    Annotation: When blood accumulates in the yin, the yin is strong and blood is substantial. The heart governs blood vessels, thus a strong yin leads to shock. When qi accumulates in the yang, the yang is strong and qi is substantial, resulting in mania.

    Blood accumulates below, qi accumulates above, causing confusion and forgetfulness.
    Annotation: When blood accumulates below, it gathers in the lower regions, leading to forgetfulness. When qi accumulates above, it rebels upwards, resulting in confusion.

    Discussion on Strange Illnesses

    The Emperor said: There is an illness that appears massive as if filled with water; palpating its pulse is large and tense, and the body feels no pain, being neither thin nor unable to eat, but eating little. What illness is this? Qibo said: The illness arises from the kidneys, known as kidney wind. Kidney wind leads to an inability to eat and is prone to shock. Once shocked, if the heart's qi is weak, death follows.
    Annotation: The foot's lesser yin cold water governs qi; a large pulse indicates wind, and a tense pulse indicates cold. In the case of water wind illness, external symptoms show bone and joint pain, yet this illness resides in the kidneys. It is not caused by external wind evils, hence there is no bodily pain. Water qi ascends, making the body not thin. Wind and water evils encroach upon the earth's qi, hence the inability to eat, and even if eating, it is not much. Being prone to shock indicates that water qi invades the heart. If after shocking, the heart's qi is weak, the heart has suffered damage from the evil.[8p]

    　　　　　阳明脉解篇

    　　黄帝问曰：足阳明之脉，病恶人与火，闻木音则惕然而惊，钟鼓不为动，闻木音而惊，何也？愿闻其故！岐伯对曰：阳明者，胃脉也。胃者土也。故闻木音而惊者，土恶木也。　　 【注　阳明之脉，乃胃之悍气，别走阳明，悍热气盛，则胃腑气虚也。】
    　　　　　气厥论

    　　脾移热于肝，则为惊衄。
    　　 【注　东方肝木。其病发惊骇，肝主血，故热甚则衄。】
    　　　　　六元正纪大论

    　　少阳之政，寅申之纪也。其病掉眩，支胁惊骇。　　 【注　诸风眩掉，皆属于肝。东方肝木，其病发惊骇。】　　少阴所至为惊惑，少阳所至为惊躁。　　 【注　此夏病之常也。】

    　　　　　血气形志篇

    　　形数惊恐，经络不通，病生于不仁，治之以按摩醪药。　　 【注　惊则气乱，恐则气下，盖血随气行，气数乱逆，则经络不通，荣卫不行，是以病生于不仁，宜按摩醪药，以行其荣卫血气焉。】[9p]

    Yangming Pulse Examination

    The Yellow Emperor asked: "The pulse of the foot Yangming indicates that one suffers from a dislike of people and fire; upon hearing the sound of wood, one is startled and frightened, whereas the sounds of bells and drums do not provoke movement. Why is this? I wish to know the reason!" Qi Bo replied: "Yangming refers to the stomach pulse. The stomach symbolizes earth. Therefore, being startled upon hearing the sound of wood signifies that earth is averse to wood."

    Discussion on Qi Stagnation

    When the spleen transfers heat to the liver, it results in sudden fright and nosebleeds.

    Great Discussion on the Six Fundamental Principles

    The governance of Shaoyang corresponds to the periods of Yin and Shen. Its ailments include dizziness and sudden fright in the sides.

    Sudden fright comes from Shaoyin, while restlessness arises from Shaoyang. This is common to summer illnesses.

    The Chapter on Blood, Qi, Form, and Will

    The state of fear and terror disrupts the channels; illness arises from a lack of benevolence. It should be treated with massage and medicinal decoctions. Fear causes disruption of qi, and terror causes qi to descend. Since blood follows the movement of qi, when qi is disordered and moving in reverse, the channels are obstructed and the nourishing and protective energies do not function, leading to sickness arising from a lack of benevolence. Thus, it is advisable to use massage and medicinal decoctions to restore the flow of nourishing and protective blood and qi.[9p]

    　　　　灵枢经

    　　　　　百病始生篇

    　　虚邪之中人也，在经之时，洒淅喜惊。　　 【注　足阳明之脉病，故惕然而喜惊也。】
    　　　　　经脉篇

    　　心主手厥阴心包络之脉，是动甚则胸胁支满，心中憺憺大动。　　 【注　甚则胸胁支满，心中憺憺大动，盖甚则有余于内也。】
    　　　　　本神篇

    　　肾盛怒而不止则伤志，志伤则喜忘其前言，腰脊不可以俯仰屈伸，毛悴色夭，死于季夏。　　【注　喜忘者，神志皆伤也。腰者肾之腑，故腰脊不可以俯仰屈伸。】
    　　　　　大惑论

    　　黄帝曰：人之善忘者，何气使然？岐伯曰：上气不足，下气有余，肠胃实而心肺虚，虚则荣卫留于下，久之不以时上，故善忘也。　　 【注　上气不足，下气有余，则肠胃实而心肺虚，虚则荣卫留于下，久之不以时上，故善忘也。】[10p]

    Classic Text of the Spiritual Pivot

    Chapter on the Origins of Diseases

    In the midst of the void and external evils, during times of abnormal occurrence, one may feel startled and joyful. [Note: This refers to diseases of the Yangming meridian, hence the startle and joy.]

    Chapter on the Meridians

    The heart governs the hand’s Jueyin meridian; when it is excessively active, it leads to fullness in the chest and ribs, and causes great agitation within the heart. [Note: When extreme, it suggests an excess within.]

    Chapter on the True Spirit

    When the kidneys are in excess and unyielding, they injure the will; when the will is injured, joy is forgotten, making it impossible to bend and stretch the waist and spine. The hair becomes frail, and the complexion pales, leading to death in late summer. [Note: Forgetting joy indicates damage to the spirit. The waist corresponds to the kidneys, hence the inability to bend and stretch.]

    Discussion on Great Confusion

    The Yellow Emperor asked: What causes a person to be prone to forgetfulness? Qibo replied: There is insufficient energy above and excess energy below; the intestines and stomach are full while the heart and lungs are deficient. When deficient, the nutrients cannot rise in time, thus causing frequent forgetfulness. [Note: The excess below coupled with deficiency above leads to fullness in the digestive organs while the heart and lungs are lacking; the stagnation prevents timely ascent of nutrients, resulting in forgetfulness.][10p]

    　　　　金匮要略 【汉　张机】

    　　　　　惊悸证治

    　　病有奔豚，有吐脓，有惊怖，有火邪，此四部病，皆从惊发得之。师曰：奔豚病从少腹起，上冲咽喉，发作欲死，复还止，皆从惊恐得之。　　病人语声寂寂然，喜惊呼者，骨节间病。　　男子面色薄者，主渴及亡血，卒喘悸。脉浮者，里虚也，虚劳里急，悸衄，腹中痛，梦失精，四肢酸疼，手足烦热，咽干口燥，小建中汤主之。　　水在肾，心下悸。
    　　病人饮水多，必暴喘满。凡食少饮多，水停心下，甚者则悸，微者短气。脉双弦者，寒也，皆大下后里虚。脉偏弦者，饮也。　　卒呕吐，心下痞，膈间有水，眩悸者，半夏加茯苓汤主之。　　寸口脉动而弱，动即为惊，弱则为悸。　　心下悸者，半夏麻黄圆主之。
    　　发汗后，脐下悸者，欲作奔豚，茯苓桂枝甘草大枣汤主之。[11p]

    Jingji Syndrome Treatment

    There are four types of diseases arising from shock: running piglet syndrome, purulent vomiting, fright, and fiery evil. All these conditions result from shock. The master said: running piglet syndrome originates from the lower abdomen, surging upward to the throat, resulting in a near-death experience followed by cessation, all stemming from fear. The patient speaks in a quiet manner, startled by sudden sounds, indicating joint issues.

    For men whose complexion is thin, this indicates thirst and blood loss, resulting in sudden palpitations. A floating pulse indicates internal deficiency; when there's weakness in the interior, it may lead to palpitations, nosebleeds, abdominal pain, loss of semen in dreams, aching limbs, heat in the hands and feet, and dryness of the throat. Xiao Jian Zhong Decoction treats this. Water resides in the kidneys, leading to palpitations beneath the heart.

    If a patient drinks excessively, they will definitely experience sudden palpitations. Generally, eating little while drinking a lot can cause water to accumulate beneath the heart; in severe cases, this leads to palpitations, while in milder cases, it results in shortness of breath. A double-string pulse indicates coldness, which signifies a significant deficiency after purging. A biased string pulse suggests fluid retention.

    For sudden vomiting, a feeling of fullness beneath the heart, and water accumulation in the diaphragm, along with dizziness and palpitations, Banxia Jia Fuling Decoction should be prescribed. A pulse that is weak and moves indicates shock; weak pulses signify palpitations. For palpitations beneath the heart, Banxia Mahuang Wan should be administered.

    After sweating, if there are palpitations below the navel suggesting running piglet syndrome, Fuling Guizhi Gancao Dazao Decoction is the appropriate remedy.[11p]

    　　　　脉诀 【晋　王叔和】

    　　　　　惊病之脉

    　　心脏歌曰：实梦忧惊怪，虚翻烟火明。　　心脉歌曰：实大相兼并有滑，舌强心惊语话难。　　虚脉歌曰：恍惚心中多悸惊，三关定息脉难成。
    　　　　千金方 【唐　孙思邈】

    　　　　　惊悸

    　　右手寸口气口以前脉阴阳俱实者，手太阴与阳明经俱实也。病苦头痛目眩，惊狂，喉痹痛，手臂卷，唇吻不收，名曰肺与大肠俱实也。
    　　左手关上脉阴阳俱虚者，足厥阴与少阳经俱虚也。病苦恍惚，尸厥不知人，妄见，少气不能言，时时自惊，名曰肝胆俱虚也。　　右手关上脉阴阳俱实者，足太阴与阳明经俱实也。病苦脾胀腹坚，抢胁下痛，胃气不转，大便难，时反泄利，腹中痛，上冲肺肝，动五脏，立喘鸣，多惊，身热汗不出，喉痹精少，名曰脾胃俱实也。　　右手寸口气口以前脉阳虚者，手阳明经也。病苦胸中喘，肠鸣，虚渴，唇干目急，善惊泄白，名曰大肠虚冷也。[12p]

    Pulse Diagnosis (by Wang Shuhe, Jin Dynasty)

    Pulse of Shock Illness

    The heart song states: "In intense dreams, there is worry from shock, but in emptiness, the flames of knowledge appear."
    The heart pulse song states: "In fullness, there is a combination of large and slippery, with a strong tongue, the heart is astonished, and speech is difficult."
    The empty pulse song states: "In bewilderment, the heart is often shaken, and at the three regions, the pulse is hard to establish."

    Thousand Gold Prescriptions (by Sun Simiao, Tang Dynasty)

    Palpitations

    When the pulse at the right wrist's cun position is full in both Yin and Yang, it indicates fullness in both the Taiyin and Yangming channels. The patient suffers from headaches, dizziness, shock, mania, throat pain, tension in the arms, and inability to close the lips; it is named fullness of both lungs and large intestine.
    When the left wrist's guan position pulse is empty in both Yin and Yang, it indicates emptiness in both the Jueyin and Shaoyang channels. The patient suffers from confusion, cannot recognize people, experiences hallucinations, has shortness of breath and inability to speak, often feeling startled; it is named emptiness of both liver and gallbladder.
    When the right wrist's guan position pulse is full in both Yin and Yang, it indicates fullness in both the Taiyin and Yangming channels. The patient suffers from abdominal fullness, hardness, pain in the flanks, stagnant stomach qi, constipation, and occasionally diarrhea, with abdominal pain, which rises to the lungs and liver, stirring the five organs, leading to wheezing, frequent shock, body heat, and inability to sweat, with throat obstruction and scanty essence; it is named fullness of both spleen and stomach.
    When the pulse at the right wrist's cun position shows Yang deficiency, it indicates the Yangming channel. The patient suffers from wheezing in the chest, bowel sounds, emptiness thirst, dry lips, urgent eyes, prone to shock and diarrhea; it is named deficiency and cold of the large intestine.[12p]

    　　左手寸口人迎以前脉阴虚者，手少阴经也。病苦悸恐不乐，心腹痛，难以言，心如寒，恍惚，名曰心虚寒也。　　夫病人卒饮水多，必暴喘满。凡食少饮多，水停心下，甚者则悸。　　诊得心积沉而芤，时上下无常处，病胸满悸，腹中热，面赤咽干，心烦，掌中热，甚则唾血，身瘈瘲，主血厥，夏瘥冬剧，色赤也。　　征音人者，主心声也。心声笑，其音竽，其志喜，其经手少阴。厥逆太阳则荣卫不通，阴阳反错，阳气外击，阴气内伤，伤则寒，寒则虚，虚则惊掣心悸，定心汤主之。[13p]

    In the diagnostic area of the left hand at the wrist, if the pulse is weak and yin is deficient, it corresponds to the hand's Lesser Yin Meridian. The patient suffers from palpitations, anxiety, and malaise, experiencing abdominal pain that is hard to express. The heart feels cold and scattered, which is termed heart deficiency-cold.

    If a patient suddenly drinks a lot of water, they will certainly suffer from violent coughing and fullness. Generally, if food intake is low and water intake is high, it leads to water accumulation under the heart, and in severe cases, this causes palpitations.

    When the diagnosis reveals a sinking and hollow heart pulse, the condition will have variable presentations, including fullness in the chest with palpitations, abdominal heat, a flushed face, dry throat, irritability, heat in the palms, and in severe cases, spitting blood, convulsions, and blood stasis. In summer, there are heat symptoms, while in winter, there are severe symptoms, presenting with a red complexion.

    The sound of the pulse indicates the state of the heart. If the heart's sound is cheerful, it has a pleasant tone; the intention is happiness, correlating to the Lesser Yin Meridian. If there is counterflow in the Sun Meridian, the protective and nourishing energies are obstructed, resulting in a reversal of yin and yang. The yang energy attacks outward, while the yin energy is injured internally, leading to coldness. Coldness leads to deficiency, which causes fright and palpitations; for this, the Calming Heart Decoction is the remedy.[13p]

    　　　　　健忘

    　　趺阳[趺阳：原作「太阳」，据《千金》卷十七肺脏脉论改。]脉浮缓，少阳脉微紧，微为血虚，紧为微寒，此为鼠乳。诊得肺积，脉浮而手按之辟易，胁下时时痛逆，背相引痛，少气善忘，目瞑结痈，皮肤寒，秋愈夏剧，主皮中时痛如虱缘之状，甚者如针刺之状，时痒色白也。　　羽音人，呻而好恚，恚而善忘，恍惚有所思，此为土克水。阳击阴，阴气伏而阳气起，起则热，热则实，实则怒，怒则忘，耳听无闻，四肢满急，小便赤黄，言音口动而不出，笑而看人，此为邪热伤肾，甚则不可治。若面黑黄，耳不应，亦可治。　　左手尺中神门以后脉阴实者，足少阴经也。病苦舌燥咽肿心烦嗌干，胸胁时痛，喘咳汗出，小腹胀满，腰背强急，体重骨热，小便赤黄，好怒好忘，足下热痛，四肢黑，耳聋，名曰肾实热也。[14p]

    Forgetfulness

    The pulse at the "Fuyang" point is floating and slow; the Shaoyang pulse is slightly tight, indicating blood deficiency. The tightness suggests slight cold, which is associated with "mouse milk." When diagnosing pulmonary accumulation, the pulse feels floating and pressing it causes discomfort. There is pain in the sides that sometimes reverses; the back feels strained and painful. Symptoms include shortness of breath, forgetfulness, closed eyelids with the formation of sores, cold skin, with conditions worsening in summer and improving in autumn. Pain occurs in the skin intermittently, resembling the sensation of lice, and in severe cases, it feels like needle pricks along with intermittent itching and a pale color.

    In people of gentle nature, they may groan and easily become angry; when angry, they tend to forget and seem lost in thought. This indicates the earth damaging water. Yang attacks yin, causing the yin energy to descend and the yang energy to rise; when it rises, it generates heat, leading to fullness, anger, and forgetfulness. They may hear without understanding; their limbs feel rushed, and their urine is reddish-yellow. Although they may speak, their words do not come out, instead they laugh while watching others—this is due to evil heat damaging the kidneys, and in severe cases, it may be untreatable. If the face appears black and yellow with unresponsive ears, treatment is still possible.

    The pulse at the "Shenmen" point on the left hand suggests fullness of yin; this corresponds to the foot's Shaoyin meridian. The patient suffers from dry tongue, swollen throat, restlessness, dry throat, intermittent pain in the chest and sides, wheezing, coughing, and sweating; the lower abdomen feels distended; the lower back is tight and painful; they feel heavy in body and bones warm; their urine is reddish-yellow, easily angered and forgetful; their feet feel hot and painful; their limbs appear dark and they suffer from deafness, which is termed kidney heat due to fullness.[14p]

    　　　　济生方 【宋　严用和】

    　　　　　论治

    　　夫惊悸者，心虚胆怯之所致也。且心者君主之官，神明出焉；胆者中正之官，决断出焉。心气安逸，胆气不怯，决断思虑，得其所矣。或因事有所大惊，或闻虚响，或见异相，登高涉险，惊忤心神，气与涎郁，遂使惊悸。惊悸不已，变生诸证，或短气悸乏，体倦自汗，四肢浮肿，饮食无味，心虚烦闷，坐卧不安，皆心虚胆怯之候也。治之之法，宁其心以壮胆气，无不瘥者矣。　　夫怔忡者，此心血不足也。盖心主于血，血乃心之主，心乃形之君，血富则心君自安矣。[15p]

    On Treatment

    The state of fright and palpitations arises from a deficiency of the heart and a lack of courage. The heart is the sovereign organ, from which the spirit emerges; courage governs decisiveness. When the heart is tranquil and the spirit is not fearful, one can think clearly and make good decisions. Sometimes, due to a significant shock, an illusory sound, or an unusual sight, one may experience fear while facing danger, which can agitate the heart and spirit, causing stagnation of energy and saliva, resulting in fright and palpitations. If fright persists, various symptoms may arise, such as shortness of breath, fatigue, sweating, swelling in the limbs, loss of appetite, agitation of the heart, and restless sitting or lying down—all signs of a deficient heart and lack of courage. The method of treatment is to calm the heart and strengthen the spirit; then, there will be no ailments left untreated. The state of disorientation indicates a deficiency of heart blood. The heart governs blood, and blood is the master of the heart; when blood is abundant, the heart can rest assured.[15p]

    多因汲汲富贵，戚戚贫贱，又思所爱，触事不意，真血虚耗，心帝失辅，渐戍怔忡。怔忡不已，变生诸症，舌强恍惚，善忧悲，少颜色，皆心病之候。《难经》云：损其心者益其荣。法当专补真血。真血若富，心帝有辅，无不愈者矣。又有冒风寒暑湿，闭塞诸经，令人怔忡；五饮停畜，堙塞中脘，亦令人怔忡。当随其证，施以治法。　　夫健忘者，常常喜忘是也。盖脾主意与思，心亦主思，思虑过度，意舍不清，神宫不职，使人健忘。洽之之法，当理心脾，使神意宁静，思则得之矣。
    　　　　河间六书 【金　刘完素】

    　　　　　惊病之因

    　　惊，心卒动而不宁也。火主于动，故心火热甚也。虽尔，止为热极于里，乃火极似水则喜惊。反兼肾水之恐者，亢则害，承乃制故也。所谓恐则喜惊者，恐则伤肾而水衰，心火自甚，故喜惊也。　　一阳一阴病发惊骇背痛噫欠，名风厥。盖胃土肝木，为木克上。风胜湿不制肾水，故令上逆。[16p]

    Many are eager to attain wealth and nobility, yet fear poverty and low status. When thoughts dwell on loved ones, unexpected events arise, causing true blood to be depleted, leading to disturbances in the heart. The mind of the sovereign loses its support, gradually causing confusion and anxiety. This persistent confusion gives rise to various ailments: a strong tongue yet foggy in perception, prone to worry and sadness, lacking vitality—these are signs of mental illness. The "Nanjing" states: "Nourishing the heart benefits its glory." Thus, one should primarily replenish true blood. When true blood is abundant, the heart has support, and there is no ailment that cannot be cured. There are also instances of catching wind, cold, heat, and humidity, which block various meridians and lead to confusion; excessive intake of liquids can stagnate the stomach, also causing confusion. One must treat according to the symptoms presented.

    As for forgetfulness, it often involves a tendency for joyful oblivion. The spleen governs intention and thoughts, while the heart also rules thinking. When thought is excessive, intentions become unclear, and the spirit's palace is not functionally active, leading to forgetfulness. The method for harmonizing this is to regulate both heart and spleen, ensuring tranquility of the spirit, thereby restoring awareness.

    Causes of Shock Illness

    Shock arises when the heart suddenly stirs and becomes unsettled. Fire is associated with movement, thus the heart fire becomes intensely hot. Nevertheless, this is merely extreme heat within; when fire reaches its peak, it resembles water, causing surprise. Conversely, when kidney water is undermined by fear, excess leads to harm; this is a matter of balance. The saying "fear leads to surprise" indicates that fear damages the kidneys and depletes water, thereby intensifying heart fire and resulting in surprise. A combination of yin and yang leading to fright results in back pain and sighing, referred to as Wind Disturbance. The stomach and spleen correspond to earth, while the liver corresponds to wood—wood overcomes earth. When wind dominates and dampness does not regulate kidney water, it causes an upward reversal.[16p]

    　　　　明理论 【金　成无己】

    　　　　　心悸

    　　伤寒悸者，何以明之？悸者，心忪是也。筑筑惕惕然动，怔怔忪忪不能自安者是矣。心悸之由，不越二种：一者气虚也，二者停饮也。伤寒二三日，心中悸而烦者，小建中汤主之。少阴病四逆，其人或悸者，四逆散加桂五分。是气虚而悸者也。饮水多，必心下悸，是停饮而悸者也。其气虚者，由阳气内弱，心下空虚，正气内动而为悸也。其停饮者，由水停心下，心为火而恶水，水既内停，心不自安则为悸也。又有汗下之后，正气内虚，邪气交击而令悸者，与气虚而悸者，则又甚焉。太阳病，发汗过多，其人叉手自冒心，心下悸。太阳病若下之，身重心下悸者，不可发汗。[17p]

    Clear Theory
    (Jin Cheng Wu Ji)

    Heart Palpitations

    In cases of heart palpitations due to cold damage, how should one clarify this? Palpitations occur when the heart is weak. When one feels anxious and cannot find peace, this defines palpitations. The causes of heart palpitations fall into two categories: one is qi deficiency, and the other is stagnant fluid. In cases of cold damage lasting two or three days, if the person experiences palpitations accompanied by restlessness, the prescription is Xiao Jian Zhong Tang. If someone with a Shaoyin condition has severe palpitations, add five grams of cinnamon to Si Ni San. This indicates palpitations due to qi deficiency. If one drinks too much water, it will inevitably lead to palpitations below the heart, indicating palpitations due to stagnant fluid. The qi deficiency occurs because of weak yang energy within, leaving the heart below empty, causing internal movement of the righteous qi, which leads to palpitations. Stagnant fluid results from water accumulating below the heart; since the heart is fire and dislikes water, when water is stationary within, the heart's inability to find peace causes palpitations. Furthermore, after sweating or purging, if the righteous qi is internally weak and the evil qi strikes against it, this can also cause palpitations. In cases of yangming disease, if excessive sweating occurs, the individual may experience palpitations with a pressed heart and the hands crossed over the chest. If yangming illness leads to purging, and the body feels heavy with palpitations below the heart, one should not induce sweating.[17p]

    少阳病不可吐下，吐下则悸而惊。少阳病不可发汗，发汗则谵语，此属胃，胃和则愈，胃不和则烦而悸。是数者，皆汗后协邪者，与其气虚而悸者，有以异也。或镇固，或化散之，皆须定其气浮也。又饮水过多，水饮不为宣布而留心下，甚者则悸。《金匮要略》曰：食少饮多，水停心下，甚者则悸。饮之为悸，甚于他邪，虽有余邪，必先治悸。何者？以水停心下，若水气散则无所不之，浸于肺则为喘为咳，传于胃则为哕为噎，溢于皮肤则为肿，渍于肠间则为利下，不可缓之也。经曰：厥而心下悸，宜先治水，与茯苓甘草汤，后治其厥。不尔，水渍于胃，必作利也。厥为邪之深者，犹先治水，况其邪气浅者乎？[18p]

    The Shao Yang disease should not be treated with vomiting or purging; doing so will lead to palpitations and fright. The Shao Yang disease should not be treated with sweating; sweating will cause delirium. This pertains to the stomach: when the stomach is harmonious, recovery occurs; when the stomach is not harmonious, there will be agitation and palpitations. These symptoms arise from the lingering邪 (evil) after sweating, and those with qi deficiency and palpitations are distinct. Some conditions require stabilization, others require dispersion, all must be assessed to see if the qi is floating.

    Additionally, excessive drinking causes water to accumulate, which can lead to palpitations. The "Essentials from the Golden Cabinet" states that when one eats little but drinks excessively, water can accumulate in the heart and lead to severe palpitations. Drinking causes palpitations more than other evils; even if other evils are present, one must first treat the palpitations. Why? Because when water accumulates in the heart, if the water vapor disperses, it can affect various organs: in the lungs, it leads to wheezing and coughing; in the stomach, it causes belching and choking; on the skin, it causes swelling; in the intestines, it leads to diarrhea. This cannot be treated lightly.

    The classics say: when there are palpitations under the heart with a cold sensation, one should first treat the water condition, using Poria and Licorice Decoction, and then treat the cold sensation. Otherwise, the water will infiltrate the stomach and cause diarrhea. When the cold sensation is of deep origin, one should still treat the water condition first; how much more so for those with a shallow evil qi![18p]

    　　　　丹溪心法 【元　朱震亨】

    　　　　　总论证治

    　　惊悸者血虚，惊悸有时，以朱砂安神丸。　　痰迷心膈者，痰药皆可，定志丸加琥珀、郁金。　　怔忡者血虚。怔忡无时，血少者多。　　有思虑便动，属虚。时作时止者，痰因火动。　　瘦人多因是血少，肥人属痰。寻常者多是痰。　　真觉心跳者是血少，四物、朱砂安神之类。　　假如病因惊而得，惊则神出其舍，舍空则痰生也。　　人之所主者心，心之所养者血。心血一虚，神气不守，此惊悸之所肇端也。曰惊曰悸，其可无辨乎？惊者恐怖之谓，悸者怔忡之谓。[19p]

    Danxi Heart Method (Yuan Dynasty - Zhu Zhenheng)

    General Discussion on Diagnosis and Treatment

    For fright and palpitations caused by blood deficiency, use Zhu Sha An Shen Wan. For phlegm obstructing the heart and diaphragm, any phlegm remedy will do, combined with Ding Zhi Wan, adding amber and turmeric. For sudden palpitations, this is also due to blood deficiency. Sudden palpitations that come and go indicate a lack of blood. Those with worries and disturbances belong to the deficient category. If it occurs intermittently, it is due to phlegm influenced by fire. Lean individuals often suffer from blood deficiency, while overweight individuals are related to phlegm. Generally, phlegm is more common. True awareness of heart palpitations indicates blood deficiency; remedies such as Si Wu and Zhu Sha An Shen can be used. If the illness arises from fright, this leads to a dispersion of the spirit; if the spirit departs, phlegm will arise. What governs a person is the heart, and what nourishes the heart is blood. When heart blood is deficient, the spirit cannot be contained, thus marking the onset of fright and palpitations. Is there no distinction between fright and palpitations? "Fright" refers to fear, while "palpitations" refer to sudden disturbances.[19p]

    心虚而郁痰，则耳闻大声，目击异物，遇险临危，触事丧志，心为之忤，使人有惕惕之状，是则为惊。心虚而停水，则胸中渗漉，虚气流动，水既上乘，心火恶之，心不自安，使人有怏怏之状，是则为悸。惊者，与之豁痰定惊之剂；悸者，与之逐水消饮之剂。所谓扶虚，不过调养心血、和平心气而已。　　健忘由精神短少者多，亦有痰者。此证皆由思忧过度，损其心胞，以致神舍不清，遇事多忘，乃思虑过度，病在心脾。又云：思伤脾亦令遗忘，治之以归脾汤，须兼理心脾，神宁意定，其证自除也。[20p]

    When the heart is vacuous and there is phlegm, one may hear loud noises and see strange objects, and in times of danger may lose resolve, causing the heart to be agitated, resulting in a state of fright. When the heart is vacuous and water stagnates, there will be seepage within the chest, and the vacuous qi flows. When the water rises to the top, the heart's fire despises it, leading to unrest in the heart, which causes a feeling of depression; this is called palpitations. For fright, one uses a formula to expel phlegm and settle fright; for palpitations, a formula to expel water and dissolve fluids should be used. What is called supporting the vacuity merely involves nourishing the heart's blood and harmonizing the heart's qi. Forgetfulness often arises from a deficiency of spirit, and in some cases, also from phlegm. These conditions result from excessive worry and anxiety, damaging the heart's nurturing, leading to unclear consciousness and frequent forgetfulness, indicating that the issue lies within the heart and spleen. It is said that overthinking harms the spleen, causing forgetfulness; thus, one can treat it with the Gui Pi Decoction, while also addressing both the heart and spleen, ensuring the spirit is tranquil and the intention settled, after which the symptoms will naturally resolve.[20p]

    　　　　医学正传 【明　虞搏】

    　　　　　惊悸怔忡

    　　《内经》曰：心者君主之官，神明出焉。夫怔忡惊悸之候，或因怒气伤肝，或因惊气入胆，母能令子虚，因而心血为之不足。又或遇事繁冗，思想无穷，则心君亦为之不宁，故神明不安，而怔忡惊悸之证作矣。夫所谓怔忡者，心中惕惕然动摇而不得安静，无时而作者是也。惊悸者，蓦然而跳跃，惊动而有欲厥之状，有时而作者是也。若夫二证之因亦有清痰积饮，留结于心胞胃口而为之者，又不可固执以为心虚，而治宜以脉证参究其的而药之，毋认非以为是也。[21p]

    Medical Transmission: On Palpitations and Anxiety

    The "Inner Canon" states: The heart is the sovereign organ, from which the spirit emerges. The conditions of anxiety and palpitations may arise either from anger harming the liver or from fright affecting the gallbladder, which can lead to insufficiency in the heart's blood. Additionally, if one encounters numerous matters and endless thoughts, the sovereign heart also becomes unsettled, causing the spirit to be disturbed, resulting in symptoms of anxiety and palpitations. The term "anxiety" refers to a restlessness in the heart that cannot find tranquility, and it occurs at all times. "Palpitations" refer to sudden jumps and racing, resulting in a feeling of impending loss of consciousness, which can appear at times. Furthermore, the causes of these two conditions may also stem from the accumulation of phlegm and fluid, which can be retained in the heart and stomach, thus leading to these symptoms. One should not rigidly assume it is solely due to a deficiency of the heart; rather, treatment should be based on the pulse and symptoms to determine its essence and address it accordingly, avoiding errors in diagnosis.[21p]

    　　　　证治要诀 【明　戴思恭】

    　　　　　总论证治

    　　惊悸者，因事有所大惊，触忤心神，气与涎郁，遂生惊悸，此乃心虚胆怯所致，宜温胆汤。呕则以人参代竹茹。若眠多异梦，随即惊觉者，宜温胆汤加酸枣仁、莲肉各一钱，以金银煎下十四友丸，或镇心丹、远志丸，酒调妙香散。　　怔忡久思所爱，触事不忘，虚耗真血，心血不足，遂成怔忡，俗谓心忡脉乱是也，宜益荣汤。　　怔忡，即忪悸也。忪悸与惊悸若相类而实不同。惊悸者，因事有所惊而悸；忪悸者本无所惊，常心忪而自悸。焉得无辨？　　感风寒暑湿闭塞诸经而忪忡，各见本门。[22p]

    Essentials of Diagnosis and Treatment
    (Ming Dynasty, Dai Sigong)

    General Discussion on Diagnosis and Treatment

    For those suffering from palpitations due to shock from events that disturb the heart and spirit, resulting in blocked qi and phlegm, this is caused by emptiness in the heart and timidity; thus, one should use Wending Decoction. If there is vomiting, replace the bamboo shavings with ginseng. If one has many strange dreams while sleeping and wakes up startled, Wending Decoction should be added with 3 grams each of sour jujube seeds and lotus flesh, boiled with Fourteen Friends Pill, or Heart-calming Pills, or Yuanshi Powder mixed with wine.

    For long-lasting thoughts about cherished matters leading to persistent anxiety, resulting in a depletion of essence and insufficient heart blood, this condition is known in common terms as palpitations and erratic pulse; thus, one should use Yirong Decoction. Palpitations, known as "zhong," can be confused with "jingqi." Although they are similar, they are fundamentally different. Palpitations occur from shocking events, while "zhong" arises from no specific shock, causing a constant state of anxiety. How can one not distinguish between them?

    Influences from wind, cold, heat, and humidity that block the meridians can also lead to anxiety; each should be addressed according to their respective categories.[22p]

    　　因痰饮怔忡者，导痰汤加炒酸枣仁，下寿星丸。　　失志者，由所求不遂，或过误自咎，懊恨嗟叹不已，独语书空，若有所失，宜温胆汤去竹茹，加人参、柏手仁各一钱，下定志丸，仍佐以酒调辰砂妙香散。　　有痞塞不饮食，心中常有所怯，爱处暗室，或倚门后，见人则惊避，似失志状，此名为卑惵之卑，以血不足故也。谷神嘉禾散加当归半钱、黄芪半钱。　　健忘者，所过之事，转盼遗忘，此乃思虑过度，病在心脾，宜归脾汤。　　健忘者，为事有始无终，言谈不知首尾，此乃病之故，非比生成之愚顽不知人事者。[23p]

    For those who experience fright due to phlegm and fluids, administer Phlegm-Transforming Decoction with fried sour jujube seeds, and follow with Shouxing Pills.

    For those who lose ambition due to unfulfilled desires, or who blame themselves for mistakes, feeling regretful and sighing endlessly, speaking to themselves as if something is lost, it is advisable to use Warm Gallbladder Decoction, remove bamboo leaves, and add one qian each of ginseng and bai shou ren, followed by Dingzhi Pills, aided with wine and the fragrant powder of cinnabar.

    In cases of chest oppression with lack of appetite, if one often feels timid in the heart, prefers dark rooms, or leans against doors, startled and avoiding others, this is known as lowly timidity due to blood deficiency. Use Gu Shen Jia He Powder, adding half a qian each of angelica and astragalus.

    For those who forget easily, losing track of events and thoughts, this is due to excessive contemplation and is a condition of the heart and spleen. It is appropriate to use Gui Pi Decoction.

    For those who forget, beginning many things but finishing none, speaking without continuity; this is due to illness, and is not merely a natural foolishness of not understanding human affairs.[23p]

    　　　　医学入门 【明　李梴】

    　　　　　总论证治

    　　思虑过度，及因大惊大恐，以致心虚停痰，或耳闻大声，目见异物，临危触事，便觉惊悸，甚则心跳欲厥，脉弦濡者，虚也。血虚，四物汤、茯神汤、妙香散、朱砂安神丸。气血俱虚，人参养荣汤、养心汤。时作时止者痰也，二陈汤加白朮、黄连、远志、竹沥、姜汁。　　怔忡因惊悸久而成，痰在下火在上故也。温胆汤加黄连、山栀、当归、贝母。气郁者，四七汤加茯神、远志、竹沥、姜汁，或十味温胆汤、金箔镇心丸。停饮，胸中漉漉有声，怏怏不安者，二陈汤加茯神、槟榔、麦门冬、沉香，或朱雀丸。惊悸二证，通用归脾汤、仁熟散、梦授天王补心丹、寿星丸、参枣丸。[24p]

    Introduction to Medicine
    [Ming Dynasty, Li Zhen]

    General Principles of Diagnosis and Treatment

    Overthinking and severe shock can lead to a deficiency of the heart, resulting in phlegm stagnation, or hearing loud sounds and seeing unusual objects may provoke fear and palpitation. In extreme cases, this can lead to a sensation of impending collapse and a weak, thready pulse, indicating deficiency. For blood deficiency, use Si Wu Decoction, Fu Shen Decoction, Miao Xiang Powder, or Zhu Sha An Shen Pills. If both qi and blood are deficient, use Ren Shen Yang Rong Decoction or Yang Xin Decoction. If symptoms appear intermittently, it is phlegm; use Er Chen Decoction with Bai Zhu, Huang Lian, Yuan Zhi, Zhu Li, and ginger juice.

    Long-lasting palpitations due to shock are caused by phlegm below and fire above. Use Wen Dan Decoction with Huang Lian, Shan Zhi, Dang Gui, and Bei Mu. For qi stagnation, use Si Qi Decoction with Fu Shen, Yuan Zhi, Zhu Li, and ginger juice, or Ten Flavor Wen Dan Decoction or Jin Bo Zhen Xin Pills. If there are symptoms of phlegm accumulation causing a rumbling sound in the chest and a feeling of unease, use Er Chen Decoction with Fu Shen, Bing Lang, Mai Men Dong, and Chen Xiang, or Zhu Que Pills.

    For the two types of palpitations, commonly used are Gui Pi Decoction, Ren Shu Powder, Meng Shou Tian Wang Bu Xin Dan, Shou Xing Pills, or Shen Zao Pills.[24p]

    　　悸，动也，心膈间客邪乘之，筑筑然触动，如人将捕，即怔忡意也。有水停心下，头眩身摇，厥而悸者，渗其水而悸厥自定。有神气素虚，心中空耗，不能自持者，有汗下后内虚而悸者，比之素虚者尤甚，须先定其气而后治其悸。大约先烦后悸者为虚，小建中汤、真武汤。脉代者，炙甘草汤入酒少许。汗后眩冒者，桂枝甘草汤。先悸后烦者为热，小柴胡汤。喜呕谵语，大便难者，小柴胡汤加大黄或加芒硝少许。谵语小便不利者，柴胡龙骨牡蛎汤。小便赤者，五苓散。　　怔忡久则健忘，皆心脾血少，神亏清气不足，证属浊气上攻，引神归舍丹主之。亦有所禀，阴魄不足，善忘者，当大补气血及定志丸。如老年神衰者，加减固本丸，通用归脾汤、仁熟散、梦授天王补心丹、寿星丸、参枣丸。[25p]

    Palpitations are movements caused by external evil energies disturbing the heart, akin to someone trying to catch something, leading to a state of confusion and anxiety. When there is water stagnating beneath the heart, dizziness and trembling occur, and if one faints and experiences palpitations, it is because the water has permeated, and the palpitations and fainting can be stabilized. Those with a weak spirit and essentially empty heart, who cannot maintain their composure, may sweat, leading to internal emptiness and palpitations which are even more severe than the just empty-hearted individuals. One must first stabilize the energy before treating the palpitations. Generally, those who feel anxious first and then have palpitations are considered deficient, and should use Xiao Jian Zhong Decoction or Zhen Wu Decoction. For those with a weak pulse, Shi Gan Cao Decoction with a little wine is appropriate. Those who feel dizzy after sweating should take Gui Zhi Gan Cao Decoction. If palpitations come before anxiety, it indicates heat, and Xiao Chai Hu Decoction is recommended. For those with a propensity to vomit, rambling speech, and difficult bowel movements, Xiao Chai Hu Decoction with a bit more Da Huang or a little Mang Xiao is indicated. For those with rambling speech and difficulty in urination, Chai Hu Long Gu Mu Li Decoction is suitable. Those with red urine should take Wu Ling San.

    If confusion persists for a long time, it leads to forgetfulness, indicating a deficiency of heart and spleen blood, and insufficient clear energy. The condition results from turbid energy rising and mistaking the spirit for the true essence. There may also be inherent deficiencies; for those prone to forgetfulness, one should greatly replenish their qi and blood and use Ding Zhi Wan. For older individuals with declining spirit, Jia Jian Gu Ben Wan should be included, additionally using Gui Pi Decoction, Ren Shu San, Meng Shou Tian Wang Bu Xin Dan, Shou Xing Wan, or Shen Jiao Wan.[25p]

    　　　　医宗必读 【明　李中梓】

    　　　　　总论证治

    　　按外有危险触之而惊，心胆强者不能为害，心胆怯者触而易惊，气郁生涎，涎与气搏，变生诸证，或短气，或自汗，并温胆汤。呕则以人参代竹茹。眠多异梦，随即惊觉，温胆汤加枣仁、莲子，以金银煎下，或镇心丹、远志丸、妙香散、琥珀养心丹、定志丸。卧多惊魇，口中有声，真珠母丸、独活汤。外物卒惊，宜行重镇，密陀僧细末茶调一钱，或黄连安神丸。或热郁生痰，寒水石散。或气郁生痰，加味四七汤。[26p]

    Essentials of Medicine by Li Zhongzi

    General Discussion on Diagnosis and Treatment

    It is noted that external dangers can cause shock; those with strong hearts and courage cannot be harmed, while those with weak hearts easily become startled. This shock may lead to phlegm due to stagnation, and when phlegm and qi clash, various symptoms may arise, such as shortness of breath or spontaneous sweating, which can be treated with the Warm Gallbladder Decoction. If there is vomiting, ginseng can be used instead of bamboo shavings. If one has numerous strange dreams causing sudden waking, add jujube seeds and lotus seeds to the Warm Gallbladder Decoction, decocted with gold and silver. Other remedies include the Tranquil Heart Pill, the Forgetting Will Pill, the Wonderful Fragrance Powder, the Amber Heart-Nourishing Pill, and the Decisive Will Pill. For frequent night terrors and vocalizations during sleep, use Mother of Pearl Pill or the Angelica Decoction. If startled unexpectedly, heavy tranquilizers should be administered; a fine powder of the mystic temple monk's herb can be mixed with tea, or the Huanglian Tranquil Heart Pill can be utilized. For heat-induced phlegm, use the Cold Water Stone Powder, or if phlegm arises from qi stagnation, add flavors to the Four-Seven Decoction.[26p]

    丹溪曰：惊则神出于舍，舍空得液，痰涎永系于胞络之间，控涎丹加辰砂、远志。　　经曰：心痹者脉不通。烦则心下鼓，盖闭而不通，病热郁而为涎，涎成则烦，心下鼓动。鼓者，跳动如击鼓也。五痹汤加茯神、远志、半夏。按经文及《原病式》云：水衰火旺，心胸躁动，天王补心丹主之。《伤寒论》曰：心为火而恶水，水停心下，筑筑然跳动，不能自安，半夏麻黄丸、茯苓饮子主之。亦有汗吐下后，正气虚而悸不得卧者，宜温胆汤。丹溪责之虚与痰，宜辰砂远志丸。[27p]

    Danxi said: When startled, the spirit leaves the dwelling, leaving it empty and allowing fluid to accumulate; phlegm and saliva are forever linked within the channels. Control the saliva using Dan with cinnabar and distant will. The classic states: When the heart is obstructed, the pulse does not flow. When agitated, the area below the heart feels like a drum, as it is closed and does not circulate. The illness is due to heat stagnating and producing saliva; when the saliva forms, there is restlessness and the area below the heart pulsates. The pulsation is akin to the beating of a drum. For the five obstruction decoction, add Fushen, distant will, and Banxia. According to the classics and the "Original Patterns of Illness": when water is deficient and fire is excessive, the chest is agitated, and the Tianwang Heart-Supplementing Pill is indicated. The "Treatise on Cold Damage" states: When the heart is fiery and dislikes water, and water is stagnant below the heart, creating a throbbing sensation, one cannot settle; deal with it using Banxia Mahuang Pill or Fuling Drink. If there has been sweating, vomiting, or purging resulting in deficiency of righteous Qi leading to palpitations and inability to lie down, Warm Gallbladder Decoction is appropriate. Danxi attributes it to deficiency and phlegm, suggesting the use of Cinnabar and Distant Will Pill.[27p]

    有饮者控涎丹。然证状不齐，总不外于心伤而火动、火郁而生涎也。若夫虚实之分，气血之辨，痰与饮，寒与热，外伤天邪，内伤情志，是在临证者详之。　　伤寒悸，乃心中筑筑然动，怔忡不安也。脉结代心悸，炙甘草汤。伤寒三四日心悸而烦，小建中汤。发汗过多，心悸喜按，桂枝甘草汤。心神不宁，怔忡不卧，安神丸。少阴病厥逆，心下悸，四逆散加桂。饮水多而悸，虽有他邪，亦先治水，茯苓甘草汤。寒热心悸，小便不利，心烦喜呕，小柴胡汤。[28p]

    Those who drink are troubled by phlegm and saliva. However, the symptoms are not uniform; they mainly stem from heart distress causing fire to rise, or stagnant fire generating phlegm. The distinctions between deficiency and excess, the differences in qi and blood, phlegm and fluid, cold and heat, as well as external injuries or internal emotional disturbances, should be thoroughly examined by the clinician.

    In cases of cold damage, when there is a pounding sensation in the heart leading to anxiety and unrest, the pulse is wiry and intermittent; prescribe Zhizhucan decoction. If after three or four days of cold damage there is heart palpitations and agitation, use Xiao Jian Zhong Tang. If sweating is excessive and there is a tendency to prefer pressure on the heart, apply Guizhi Gan Cao Tang. For unsettled mind, restlessness, and inability to sleep, use An Shen Wan. In lesser yin disorder with reversal and palpitations below the heart, add Gui to Si Ni San. If there is excessive drinking and palpitations, despite other pathogenic influences, first treat the fluid retention with Fuling Gan Cao Tang. For palpitations with cold and heat, difficulty in urination, and irritability with a tendency to vomit, use Xiao Chai Hu Tang.[28p]

    少阳发汗，谵语悸动，小柴胡汤。寸口脉动为惊，凡惊者其脉止而复来，其人目睛不转，不能呼气。　　按《内经》健忘之原，俱责之心肾不交，心不下交于肾，浊火乱其神明，肾不上交于心，精气因而不用，火居上则因而为痰，水居下则因而生躁，扰扰纭纭，昏而不宁，故补肾而使之时上，养心而使之善下，则神气清明，志意常治，而何健忘之有？思虑过度，归脾汤。精神衰倦，人参养荣汤、宁志膏。痰迷心窍，导痰汤送寿星丸。心肾不交，朱雀丸。[29p]

    Lesser Yang causes sweating, accompanied by delirium and palpitations, treated with Xiao Chai Hu Decoction. The pulse at the inch position is agitated; generally, during fright, the pulse stops and then returns. The person's eyes do not move, and they are unable to breathe out. According to the "Inner Canon," the origin of forgetfulness is attributable to the failure of the heart and kidneys to communicate. The heart does not descend to connect with the kidneys, causing turbidity and chaos in the spirit. The kidneys do not ascend to connect with the heart, leading to a lack of vital energy. When fire remains above, it causes phlegm; when water is below, it results in restlessness. Thus, there is confusion, and one cannot attain tranquility. Therefore, tonifying the kidneys and allowing them to rise, nourishing the heart and enabling its proper descent can lead to clarity of spirit and stable intent, eliminating forgetfulness. Overthinking is addressed with Gui Pi Decoction. Mental fatigue is treated with Ren Shen Yang Rong Decoction and Ning Zhi Ointment. Phlegm obstructing the heart orifices is remedied by guiding phlegm decoction paired with Shou Xing Pills. For the failure of heart and kidney communication, Zhu Que Pill is used.[29p]

    　　　　证治准绳 【明　王肯堂】

    　　　　　总论证治

    　　或问惊悸怔忡恐怖之别，曰：悸即怔忡也。怔忡者，本无所惊，自心动而不宁。惊者，因外有所触而卒动。张子和云：惊者为自不知故也；恐者为自知也。盖惊者闻响即惊，恐者自知，如人将捕之状，及不能独自坐卧，必须人为伴侣，方不恐惧，或夜必用灯照，无灯烛亦恐惧者是也。　　《内经》无有称惊怖者，始于《金匮要略》奔豚条云：有惊怖继之；云：惊恐由是而见。惊怖即惊恐怖惧也，恐亦惧也，于义且同。凡连称其名以为提纲者，多是一阴一阳对待而言。如喜怒并称者，喜出于心，心居于阳，怒出于肝，肝居于阴。志意并称者，志是静而不移，意是动而不定。静则阴也，动则阳也。[30p]

    Principles of Diagnosis and Treatment (Ming Dynasty, Wang Kentang)

    General Discussion on Diagnosis and Treatment

    Someone asked about the distinctions between agitation, palpitations, and fear, and it was said: Palpitations are the same as agitation. Agitation, in essence, arises from a lack of calmness within the heart. Surprise, on the other hand, is caused by an external stimulus. Zhang Zihe said: Surprise results from ignorance of oneself; fear arises from self-awareness. Indeed, surprise occurs when one hears a sound causing alarm, while fear comes from self-awareness, as in the case when one feels they might be caught and cannot sit or lie down alone without needing a companion to feel secure. Some might even need a light at night; if no candle or lamp is available, they feel fear. The "Inner Classic" does not mention surprise and fear, as it begins from the "Golden Coffer Prescriptions," which states: "There is surprise followed by fear"; it adds that surprise and fear become apparent. Surprise and fear refer to the same concept of alarm and dread, and fear also implies apprehension, thus sharing a similar meaning. Generally, when both names are mentioned together as a framework, it pertains to the interplay of yin and yang. For instance, when joy and anger are mentioned together, joy emanates from the heart (yang), while anger arises from the liver (yin). When will and intention are discussed together, will is static and unchanging (yin), while intention is dynamic and unstable (yang). Static indicates yin, while dynamic indicates yang.[30p]

    惊恐并称者，惊因触于外事，内动其心，心动则神摇；恐因惑于外事，内慊其志，志慊则精却。是故《内经》谓：惊则心无所依，神无所归，虑无所定，故气乱矣。恐则精却，却则上焦闭，闭则无气还，无气还则下焦胀，故气不行矣。又谓：尝贵后贱，尝富后贫，悲忧内结，至于脱营失精，病深无气，则洒然而惊。此类皆是病从外事而动内之心神者也。若夫在身之阴阳衰盛，而致惊恐者，惊是火热烁动其心，心动则神乱，神用无方，故惊之变态，亦不一状，随其所之，与五神相应而动。肝藏魂，魂不安则为惊骇，为惊妄。肺藏魄，魄不安则惊躁。脾藏意，意不专则惊惑。肾藏志，志慊则惊恐，心惕惕然。胃虽无神，然为五脏之海，诸热归之，则发惊狂，若闻木音，则惕然心欲动也。恐者，则是热伤其肾，肾伤则精虚，精虚则志不足，志本一定而不移，故恐亦无他状。[31p]

    Fear and shock arise when external events disturb the inner mind. When the heart is moved, the spirit becomes unsettled; when there is confusion from outside, it frustrates one's aspirations, leading to a retreat of one's essence. Thus, in the Inner Canon it is said: when shocked, the heart has nowhere to rely on, the spirit has nowhere to return, and thoughts cannot settle, causing the qi to be disrupted. In fear, the essence retreats, leading to the closure of the upper burner; when closed, there is no qi returning; without qi returning, the lower burner becomes swollen, causing the qi to stagnate. It is also said: experiencing wealth after poverty or distress after happiness, sorrow and worry being internally bound, may lead to the loss of essence and a deep-rooted illness with insufficient qi, resulting in a sudden shock. Such cases are all illnesses that arise from external events disturbing the inner heart and spirit.

    As for the internal balance of yin and yang affecting shock and fear, shock is caused by fire and heat agitating the heart; when the heart is disturbed, the spirit becomes chaotic, and the spirit’s use lacks direction. Thus, the manifestations of shock vary and depend on the individual, corresponding with the five spirits. The liver houses the hun (ethereal soul); when the hun is unsettled, it causes alarm and delusion. The lung houses the po (corporal soul); when the po is restless, it leads to agitation. The spleen houses the yi (intellect); when the yi is not focused, it causes confusion. The kidney houses will; when the will is frustrated, it leads to fear and trepidation. Although the stomach has no spirit, it is considered the sea of the five organs; when numerous heat energies return to it, it results in shock and mania. For instance, upon hearing the sound of wood, the heart may tremble and yearn to move. Fear, then, arises as heat injures the kidneys; when the kidneys are harmed, the essence becomes deficient; when the essence is deficient, there is insufficient will. Since the will is originally steady and unchanging, fear does not exhibit other forms.[31p]

    《内经》于惊之病邪，有火热二淫，司天在泉胜复之气，有各经热病所致，有三阳积并，有气并于阳，皆为诸惊等病。故病机统而言曰：诸病惊骇，皆属于火也。于恐病之邪者，有精气并于肾则恐，有血不足则恐，有阴少阳入阴阳相搏则恐，有胃气热肾气微弱则恐，肾是动病则恐。然于肝之惊恐互相作者，以其脏气属阳居阴，纳血藏魂，魂不安则神动，神动则惊；血不足则志慊，志慊则恐。故二者肝脏兼而有之。似此之类，于火热二淫，属外感之邪。余者之惊恐，皆因人气之阴阳所动而内生者也。虽然，亦非独火热二淫而已。于阳明脉急，则亦为惊矣。曰：惊恐二病，与内外所因，其治法同乎异乎？曰：惊则安其神，恐则定其志，治当分阴阳之别，何得而同也？夫易之为卦，乾坤交，坎离列，坎离交而后为既济，而人以五脏应之。[32p]

    In the "Inner Canon," regarding the disease caused by shock, there are two types of heat and fire. The qi of the celestial controller is related to the reaction of the springs, which leads to various heat-related illnesses in different channels, as well as the accumulation of the three yang and the qi combining with the yang, all of which contribute to shock and similar ailments. Therefore, in a general sense, it is said that all diseases of shock derive from fire.

    For the fear-induced illness, it arises from the essence and qi combining in the kidneys, leading to fear. A deficiency in blood can also cause fear. If there is a deficiency in yin, the yang will intrude upon it, causing them to clash, resulting in fear. Furthermore, if the stomach qi is hot and the kidney qi is weak, fear can occur, regardless of whether the kidneys are compromised.

    However, when the liver is involved, the shock and fear may interact, as the liver’s qi belongs to the yang while residing in the yin, storing blood and the soul. If the soul is unsettled, the spirit becomes agitated; when the spirit is agitated, shock occurs. A deficiency in blood leads to discontent, and discontent leads to fear. Hence, both conditions are attributed to the liver.

    Similar situations arise from the two types of heat, attributed to external pathogenic influences. Other forms of shock and fear arise from the internal fluctuations of a person's qi in relation to yin and yang. However, it is not solely about the two forms of heat. When there is a rapid pulse in the yangming channel, this too can induce shock.

    It is queried whether the diseases of shock and fear, arising from internal and external causes, have the same or different treatment methods. It is stated that for shock, one should pacify the spirit; for fear, one should stabilize the will. Treatment should distinguish between yin and yang, hence they cannot be treated alike.

    The changes in the I Ching depict the interaction of the heavens and the earth, with the hexagrams of Kan and Li arranged, leading to their interplay resulting in a completed state, corresponding to the five organs of the human body.[32p]

    心为离火，内阴而外阳；肾为坎水，内阳而外阴。内者是主，外者是用。又主内者五神，外用者五气。是故心以神为主，阳为用；肾以志为主，阴为用。阳则气也，火也；阴则精也，水也。及乎水火既济，全在阴精上奉以养其神，阳气下藏以定其志。不然，则神摇不安于内，阳气散于外，志感于中，阴精走于下，既有二脏水火之分，治法安得无少异？所以惊者，必先安其神，然后散乱之气可敛，气敛则阳道行矣。恐者必先定其志，然后走失之精可固，精固则阴气用矣。于药而有二脏君臣佐使之殊用，内外所感者亦少异焉。为外事惊者，虽子和氏谓惊者平之，平常也，使病者时时闻之习熟，自然不惊，固是良法，不若使其平心易气以先之，而后药之也。吾谓内气动其神者，则不可用张氏之法，唯当以药平其阴阳之盛衰，而后神可安志可定矣。[33p]

    The heart represents the fire of separation, with inward yin and outward yang; the kidney represents the water of the abyss, with inward yang and outward yin. The internal is the master, and the external is the application. The internal masters are the five spirits, while the external applications are the five energies. Therefore, the heart governs with the spirit as the master and uses yang; the kidney governs with will as the master and uses yin. Yang corresponds to qi and fire; yin corresponds to essence and water. When water and fire are harmonized, it all relies on nourishing the spirit with yin essence, while storing yang qi below to stabilize the will. Otherwise, the spirit will be restless internally, yang qi will disperse externally, the will will be disturbed internally, and yin essence will flee below, and with the distinction between the two organ's water and fire, how can the treatment not differ in some way? Thus, for those who are startled, one must first calm their spirit; only then can the scattered qi be gathered. When qi is gathered, the yang pathway can function. For those who are fearful, one must first stabilize their will; only then can the fleeing essence be secured. When essence is secured, the yin qi can function. Regarding medicine, the two organs have distinct roles as sovereign, minister, and assistants in their usage, and the effects felt from the internal and external are not so different. For those startled by external matters, although Ziheshi mentions that the startled should be made calm, which is common practice, allowing the patient to hear and become accustomed to it so that they are naturally unstartled is indeed a good method. However, it is better to bring peace to the heart and ease the qi beforehand, and then use medicine. I say that, for internal qi affecting the spirit, one should not employ Zhang’s method but should instead use medicine to balance the rise and fall of yin and yang, after which the spirit can be calmed and the will can be stabilized.[33p]

    《伤寒明理论》释悸字云：悸，心忪也，筑筑惕惕然动，怔怔忪忪不能自安也。则悸即怔忡。而今人分为两条，谬矣。心悸之由，不越二种，一者虚也，二者饮也。气虚者，由阳气内虚，心下空虚，火气内动而为悸也。血虚者亦然。其停饮者，由水停心下，心为火而恶水，水既内停，心不自安，故为悸也。有汗吐下后，正气内虚而悸者；有邪气交击而悸者；有荣卫涸流脉结代者，则又甚焉。必生津液益血以实其虚，此从伤寒而论者。若杂病，则考诸《内经》云：心痹者，脉不通，烦则心下鼓。胆病者，口苦呕宿汁，心下憺憺恐，如人将捕之状。足阳明是动，闻木音则惕然而惊；心包络是动，病心中憺憺大动；肾是动，病善恐，心惕然然如人将捕之。[34p]

    In the "Theory of Febrile Diseases," the character for "palpitation" is explained as follows: The term "palpitation" refers to the heart being anxious, causing a feeling of restlessness and agitation, leading to an inability to find peace. Therefore, palpitation is synonymous with fright and agitation. However, modern interpretations divide this into two categories, which is incorrect. The causes of heart palpitations fall into two types: one is deficiency, and the other is excess intake.

    In cases of qi deficiency, it arises from the internal weakness of yang qi, resulting in an empty heart space where the internal heat causes palpitations. The same applies to blood deficiency. Cases of fluid retention occur when water stagnates below the heart, where the heart, being related to fire, repels water. When water is stagnant, the heart cannot find peace, resulting in palpitations.

    After sweating, vomiting, or purging, if the vital energy is internally deficient, palpitations may occur; if there is an invasion of pathogenic energy, palpitations may also arise; and if there is a depletion of the nourishing and defending energies leading to pulse irregularities, the condition worsens. It is essential to generate bodily fluids and nourish blood to alleviate deficiency, especially when discussing febrile diseases.

    Regarding mixed diseases, one may refer to the "Inner Canon," which states that in heart obstruction, there is a lack of pulse circulation, leading to discomfort in the chest. In cases of gallbladder disease, symptoms include bitter taste in the mouth, vomiting of residual bile, and a feeling of fear and anxiety as if one is about to be captured. The yangming channel is associated with movement; upon hearing wood sounds, one may feel startled; the pericardium is also linked to movement, with symptoms manifesting as great agitation in the heart; the kidneys relate to movement as well, presenting with heightened feelings of fear, resembling the sensation of impending capture.[34p]

    《原病式》云：因水衰火旺，其心胸躁动，谓之怔忡。然后知悸之为病，是心脏之气不得其正，动而为火邪者也。盖心为君火，包络为相火。火为阳，阳主动。君火之下，阴精承之；相火之下，水气承之。夫如是而动，则得其正，而清净光明，为生之气也。若乏所承，则君火过而不正，变为烦热，相火妄动，既热且动，岂不见心悸之证哉？况心者神明居之，经曰两精相搏谓之神，又曰血气者人之神，则是阴阳气血，在心脏未始相离也。今失其阴，偏倾于阳，阳亦以失所承而散乱，故精神怔怔忡忡不能自安矣。如是者，当自心脏中补其不足之心血，以安其神气；不已，则求其属以衰之，壮水之主以制阳光也。又包络之火，非惟辅心，而且游行于五脏，故五脏之气妄动者，皆火也。是以各脏有疾，皆能与包络之火，合动而作悸。[35p]

    The "Yuan Bing Shi" states: When water diminishes and fire rises, the heart and chest become agitated, which is termed "zhengchong" (anxiety). Then it is understood that palpitations are a sickness, stemming from the heart's energy being out of balance, with movements creating fire pathogens. The heart is the lord fire, and the pericardium is the minister fire. Fire is yang, and yang is active. Below the lord fire, the yin essence supports it; below the minister fire, the water qi supports it. When these energies move correctly, they maintain purity and brightness, vital for life. If there is a lack of support, the lord fire becomes excessive and unbalanced, turning into restlessness and heat, while the minister fire moves erratically, bringing about both heat and motion. Is it not evident that this leads to symptoms of palpitations? Moreover, the heart is where the spirit resides. The classics say that the interaction of the two essences is termed spirit, and also state that blood and qi are the spirit of a person, indicating that yin and yang, qi and blood, are never separate from the heart. If one loses the yin, tilting towards yang, the yang becomes disorganized and scattered due to the loss of its support, thus the spirit becomes unsettled and anxious. In such cases, one should replenish the deficient heart blood from within the heart to soothe the spirit; if this fails, one should seek to weaken the excess while reinforcing the water element to restrain the yang energy. Furthermore, the fire of the pericardium not only aids the heart but also circulates in the five organs; hence, any erratic movement of qi in the organs is also due to fire. Therefore, when each organ is ill, they can all act in concert with the fire of the pericardium, causing palpitations.[35p]

    如是者，当自各脏补泻其火起之由，而后从包络调之平之，随其攸利而治。若各脏移热于心，而致包络之火动者，治亦如之。若心气不足，肾水陵之，逆上而停心者，必折其逆气，泻其水，补其阳。若左肾之真水不足，而右肾之火上逆，与包络合动者，必峻补左肾之阴以制之。若内外诸邪，郁其二火，不得发越，隔绝荣卫，不得充养其正气者，则皆以治邪解郁为主。若痰饮停于中焦，碍其经络，不得舒通，而郁火与痰相击于心下，以为怔忡者，必导去其痰，经脉行则病自已。　　人生气禀不同，得气之清则心之知觉者明，得气之浊则心之知觉者昏。心之明者，无有限量，虽千百世已往之事，一过目则终身记而不忘，岂得忘其目前者乎？心之昏者，精神既短，则目前不待于伤心，而不能追忆其事矣。[36p]

    In such cases, one should identify the source of the heat arising from each organ, and thereafter adjust and balance the protective layer according to what is beneficial for treatment. If the heat from various organs moves to the heart and causes the fire of the protective layer to ignite, the treatment should also follow this principle. If the heart's qi is insufficient, and the kidney's water surges upward to stagnate in the heart, it is necessary to overcome the counteracting qi, drain excess water, and nourish the yang. If the true water of the left kidney is insufficient, and the fire of the right kidney rises and interacts with the protective layer, one must vigorously replenish the yin of the left kidney to counteract it. If internal and external evils stifle the two fires, preventing them from surging forth and blocking the nourishment of the correct qi, treatment should primarily focus on dispelling the evils and resolving the stagnation. If phlegm and fluid stagnate in the middle-jiao, obstructing the meridians and preventing smooth flow, and if the stifled fire collides with phlegm beneath the heart, causing palpitations, one must clear the phlegm, and once the meridians are flowing, the illness will resolve.

    Human temperament is inherently different; when one obtains clear qi, the heart’s perception is bright, while when one acquires turbid qi, the heart’s perception becomes dull. The clarity of the heart has no limits; even matters from a thousand or a hundred generations past, once seen, will be remembered for a lifetime and not forgotten—how could one forget what is currently at hand? Conversely, the dullness of the heart results in limited spirit; thus, in the face of current matters, one cannot recall past events.[36p]

    刘河间谓水清明而火昏浊，故上善若水，下愚若火，此禀质使之然也。设禀质浊混者，则不耐于事物之扰，扰则失其灵而健忘也。盖气与血，人之神也。经曰：静则神藏，躁则消亡。静乃水之体，躁乃火之用。故性静则心存乎中，情动则心忘于外，动不已则忘亦不已，忘不已则存乎中者几希，存乎中者几希则语后便忘，不俟终日已。所以世人多忘者，役役扰扰，纷纭交错，当事于一生，其气血之阴者将竭，必禀质在中人以上，清明有所守，不为事物所乱者，百难一人也。由是言之，药固有安心养血之功，不若平其心，易其气，养其在己而已。若夫痰之健忘，乃一时之病，然病忘之邪，非独痰也。凡其心有所寄，与诸火热伤乱其心者，皆得健忘，如《灵枢》谓：盛怒伤志，志伤善忘。《内经》谓：血并于下，气并于上，乱而善忘。夫如是，岂可不各从所由而为治耶？[37p]

    Liu Hejian stated that water is clear and bright while fire is dark and turbid, hence the highest virtue resembles water, while the lowest folly resembles fire; this is due to inherent qualities. If one's disposition is muddled, they cannot endure the disturbances of the world, and when disturbed, they lose their spirit and become forgetful. Indeed, qi and blood are the essence of a person. The classics say: "In tranquility, the spirit is hidden; in agitation, it dissipates." Tranquility is the nature of water, while agitation is the function of fire. Therefore, when one's nature is tranquil, the heart remains centered; when emotions stir, the heart forgets the inside and becomes distracted by the outside. If agitation does not cease, forgetfulness also continues; if forgetfulness persists, the essence within becomes rare. If the essence within becomes rare, one often forgets the spoken words, even before a day has passed. Thus, many in the world forget because they are preoccupied, disturbed, and entangled in the affairs of life; their qi and blood become depleted, particularly if one's inherent qualities are above the average, and they maintain clarity that is not disturbed by external affairs, such a person is exceedingly rare.

    From this, it can be inferred that while medicine certainly has the function of calming the heart and nourishing the blood, it is less effective than achieving peace of mind, easing one's qi, and nurturing one's inner self. On the other hand, forgetfulness linked to phlegm is a temporary ailment; however, the causes of forgetfulness are not solely phlegm. Anything that the heart is attached to, combined with the heat of various fires that disrupts the heart, can lead to forgetfulness. As stated in the "Lingshu," great anger harms the will, and the will suffers from forgetfulness. The "Neijing" says: "Blood gathers below while qi gathers above; when in chaos, forgetfulness ensues." In this case, how can one not address each cause separately for treatment?[37p]

    　　　　景岳全书 【明　张介宾】

    　　　　　论证

    　　怔忡之病，心胸筑筑振动，惶惶惕惕，无时得宁者是也？然古无是名，在《内经》则曰，胃之大络名曰虚里，出于左乳下，其动应衣，宗气泄也。在越人、仲景则有动气在上下左右之辨，云诸动气皆不可汗下也。凡此者，即皆怔忡之类。此证惟阴虚劳损之人乃有之。盖阴虚于下，则宗气无根，而气不归源，所以在上则浮撼于胸臆，在下则振动于脐旁。虚微者动亦微，虚甚者动亦甚。凡患此者，速宜节欲节劳，切戒酒色。凡治此者，速宜养气养精，滋培根本。若或误认为痰火而妄施清利，则速其危矣。　　惊有二证：有因病而惊者，有因惊而病者。如东方色青，入通于肝，其病发惊骇；及伤寒阳明证，闻木音则惕然而惊之类。[38p]

    On Proof

    The ailment of frightful palpitations is characterized by a trembling heart and chest, a continual state of alarm and fear, leaving one unable to find peace at any time. However, in ancient times, there was no such name for this condition. In the "Inner Canon," it describes a major channel of the stomach called "Xu Li," located beneath the left breast, whose movement corresponds to clothing and represents a leakage of vital energy. In the texts of the Yue people and Zhongjing, there is a differentiation of moving energies in the upper and lower regions, stating that all such energies should not be sweated out. All these conditions are indeed types of frightful palpitations. This symptom is only found in those who suffer from Yin deficiency and overexertion. When Yin is deficient below, the vital energy has no root, and so it does not return to its source; thus, it floats and shakes in the chest above and vibrates beside the navel below. Those with mild deficiency will experience minor movements, while those with severe deficiency will experience intense movements. Those afflicted should promptly regulate desires and labor, and strictly abstain from alcohol and sensual pleasures. In treatment, one should promptly nurture energy and essence and reinforce the foundation. If one mistakenly believes this to be phlegm-fire and mistakenly implements purging treatments, it will hasten their danger.

    There are two types of fright: one that arises from illness and one that arises from fright leading to illness. For example, when the eastern color is green, it communicates with the liver, causing alarming symptoms; also, in cases of cold damage to the Yangming, hearing the sound of wood can cause sudden fright.[38p]

    此则或因岁火之盛，或因岁木之衰，或因风热之相搏，或因金木之相制，是当察客邪以兼治其标。若因惊而病者，如惊则气乱而心无所倚，神无所归，虑无所定之类，此必于闻见夺气而得之，是宜安养心神，滋培肝胆，当以专抉元气为主。治此固有二者之辨，然总之主气强者不易惊，而易惊者必肝胆之不足者也。故虽有客邪，亦当知先本后标之义。　　又如惊则气乱，恐则气下。惊恐虽若同类，而不知恐之伤人，尤甚于惊。何也？盖惊出于暂，而暂者即可复；恐积于渐，而渐者不可解。甚至心怯而神伤，精却则阴痿，日消月缩，不亡不已。此非大勇大断者，必不能拔去其病根，徒资药力，不易及也。予尝治暴惊者十愈其八九，治恐惧者十不得其一二。[39p]

    This may be due to the excessive fire of the year, or the decline of wood that year, or the conflict between wind and heat, or the interplay between metal and wood. One must examine the external pathogens and simultaneously treat the symptoms. If a person becomes ill from being startled, it is because the shock disrupts the qi, leaving the heart unsupported, the spirit unfocused, and the mind unsettled. This distress must arise from the loss of qi through sights and sounds. Thus, it is advisable to nurture the heart and spirit, and bolster the liver and gallbladder, focusing primarily on restoring the original qi.

    In treating this, there is a distinction to be made; generally, those with strong qi are not easily startled, while those easily startled typically have insufficient liver and gallbladder strength. Therefore, even in the presence of external pathogens, one must understand the importance of addressing the root cause before the symptoms.

    Moreover, when startled, the qi becomes chaotic; when fearful, the qi descends. Although fright and fear seem similar, the harm from fear is particularly severe compared to that from shock. Why? Because fright occurs suddenly and can be quickly resolved; fear accumulates gradually and cannot easily be dispelled. It can even lead to timidity and damage the spirit, causing an erosion of essence, which diminishes day by day, without cessation until death ensues. Only those with great courage and determination can uproot the root of this illness; merely relying on medicinal power is insufficient. I have treated ten cases of acute fright, with eight or nine fully recovering, while treatments for fear and anxiety have resulted in success for only one or two out of ten.[39p]

    　　　　　论治

    　　凡治怔忡惊恐者，虽有心脾肝肾之分，然阳统乎阴，心本乎肾，所以上不宁者未有不由乎下，心气虚者未有不因乎精，此心肝脾肾之气，名虽有异，而治有不可离者，亦以精气互根之宜然，而君相相资之全力也。然或宜先气而后精，或宜先精而后气，或兼热者之宜清，或兼寒者之宜暖，此又当因其病情而酌用之。故用方者，宜圆不宜凿也。　　心脾血气本虚，而或为怔忡，或为惊恐，或偶以大惊猝恐，而致神志昏乱者，俱宜七福饮，甚者大补元煎。若命门水亏，真阴不足，而怔忡不已者，左归饮。若命门火亏，真阳不足而怔忡者，右归饮。若三阴精血亏损，阴中之阳不足，而为怔忡惊恐者，大营煎或理阴煎。[40p]

    Discussion on Treatment

    For those suffering from fright, panic, and anxiety, although there are distinctions between the heart, spleen, liver, and kidneys, the yang governs the yin, and the heart is fundamentally rooted in the kidneys. Thus, when there is unrest above, it is invariably influenced by conditions below. When the heart's energy is deficient, it is always due to a deficiency in essence. This energy from the heart, liver, spleen, and kidneys, despite their different names, is interrelated in treatment, due to the mutual roots of essence and energy, and the complete strength of the monarch and minister; however, sometimes it is advisable to prioritize energy over essence, or essence over energy. In some cases, where there is heat, it is better to clear it; where there is cold, it is better to warm it. This should also depend on the specific condition of the illness. Therefore, when utilizing formulas, they should be holistic, not hewn down to specifics.

    When there is a deficiency in heart and spleen blood and energy, manifesting as fright, panic, or occasional severe shock leading to confusion of mind, the suitable remedy is the Seven Fortune Decoction, or in more severe cases, the Great Replenishing Decoction. If there is deficiency in the gate of life’s water, and true yin is insufficient, leading to persistent fright, the Left Return Decoction is appropriate. Conversely, if there is deficiency in the gate of life’s fire, and true yang is insufficient resulting in fright, the Right Return Decoction is indicated. If the three yin, essence, and blood are depleted, and there is insufficient yang within the yin leading to fright and panic, the Great Nutrient Decoction or the Regulating Yin Decoction should be used.[40p]

    若水亏火盛，烦躁热渴而怔忡惊悸不宁者，二阴煎，或加减一阴煎。若思郁过度，耗伤心血，而为怔忡惊悸者，逍遥饮或益营汤。若寒痰停畜心下而怔忡者，姜朮汤。　　心虚血少，神志不宁而惊悸者，养心汤或宁志丸或十四友丸。若因惊失志而心神不宁者，宁志膏或远志丸。心血不足，肝火不清，血热多惊者，朱砂安神丸，心神虚怯，微兼痰火而惊悸者，八物定志丸。心气郁滞，多痰而惊者，加味四七汤。痰迷心窍惊悸者，温胆汤或茯苓饮子；甚者朱砂消痰饮。风热生痰，上乘心膈而惊悸者，简要济众方。　　若大恐大惧以致伤损心脾肾气，而神消精却，饮食日减者，必用七福饮、理阴煎或大营煎或大补元煎之类，酌宜治之。然必洗心涤虑，尽释病根，则庶可保全也。[41p]

    If water is deficient and fire is excessive, causing agitation, heat, thirst, and restlessness, then administer the Er Yin decoction, possibly adjusting it with one more yin decoction. If excessive worry leads to damage of heart blood, resulting in agitation and fright, then use the Xiaoyao drink or the Yiying soup. If cold phlegm is stuck beneath the heart, causing agitation, then use the Jiangzhur decoction.

    If heart deficiency and blood scarcity lead to unrest and fright, then use the Yangxin soup or the Ningzhi pill or the Shisiyou pill. If fear causes loss of spirit and unrest of the mind, then use the Ningzhi paste or the Yuanzhi pill. If there is insufficient heart blood and unclear liver fire, leading to excessive fright from heat, then use the Zhusha Anshen pill. If there is a deficiency of heart spirit and slight phlegm fire, resulting in agitation, then use the Bawudi Dingzhi pill.

    If qi is stagnated in the heart with excessive phlegm leading to fright, then add the modified Siqi decoction. If phlegm obstructs the heart leading to fright, then administer the Wendan decoction or the Fuling drink; in severe cases, use the Zhushaxiao phlegm drink. If wind-heat generates phlegm that rises and causes fright, use the Jianyao Jizhong formula.

    If great fear and terror damage the qi of the heart, spleen, and kidneys, resulting in depletion of spirit and essence, and a gradual decrease in appetite, then it is essential to use the Qifuding, Liyin decoction, or the Daying decoction, or the Dabuyuan decoction as necessary. However, it is vital to cleanse the heart and settle the thoughts to fully dispel the root of the illness, in order to ensure preservation of health.[41p]

    　　　　石室秘箓 【清　陈士铎】

    　　　　　论治法

    　　心惊非心病也，乃肝血虚而不能养心也。方用白芍、当归、麦冬、熟地各五钱，生枣仁一两，茯神三钱，北五味、远志各一钱，人参二钱，水煎服。此方之妙，全不去治心，治肝正所以治心，治肺正所以益心也。　　肾，水脏也；心，火脏也。是心肾二经为雠敌，似乎不宜牵连而一治之。不知心肾虽相克，其实相须。无心之火则成死灰，无肾之水则成冰炭。心必得肾水以滋养，肾必得心火而温暖。如人惊惕不安，岂非心肾不交乎？人以为惊惕不安，心之病，我以为肾之病，非颠倒之也，实至当不易之理。[42p]

    Discussion on Treatment Methods

    Anxiety is not a disease of the heart; rather, it is due to the deficiency of liver blood that cannot nourish the heart. The prescription includes five cents each of white peony, angelica, ophiopogon, and cooked rehmannia, one tael of sour jujube seed, three cents of poria, one cent each of north cornelian cherry and distant will, and two cents of ginseng, to be boiled in water and taken as a decoction. The brilliance of this formula lies in not specifically treating the heart; treating the liver is precisely how to treat the heart, and treating the lung benefits the heart.

    The kidney is the water organ; the heart is the fire organ. These two meridians, the heart and kidney, seem to be adversaries and ought not to be treated together. However, although the heart and kidney oppose each other, they actually rely on one another. Without the heart's fire, it becomes dead ash; without the kidney's water, it turns into ice and charcoal. The heart must receive kidney water to be nourished, and the kidney must have heart fire to be warmed. When a person is anxious and restless, isn’t it due to the heart and kidney not connecting? While others might consider anxiety and unrest as a heart issue, I view it as a kidney issue—not a reversal of logic, but rather a principle that is truly not easily overlooked.[42p]

    方用白朮、芡实、橘红、熟地各五两，人参、枣仁、炒山药、柏子仁去油、茯神、山茱萸、麦冬各三两，北五味、远志、菖蒲各一两，砂仁三钱，各为末，蜜为丸，白滚水送下五钱。此丸之妙，乃治肾之药，少于治心，盖心君宁静，肾气自安，肾气既安，何至心动？此治心正所以治肾，而治肾正所以治心也。　　心经之病，怔忡不寐等证，乃心血少也。方用人参、麦冬、茯神、当归各三钱，丹参二钱，生枣仁、熟枣仁各五钱，菖蒲、甘草、五味子各一钱，水煎服。此方之妙，妙在生熟枣仁各五钱，而以诸补心之药为佐使。盖枣仁乃安心治不寐之圣药，生用使其日间不卧，熟用使其夜间不醒也。[43p]

    The recipe uses five taels each of white atractylodes, lotus seed, tangerine peel, and cooked rehmannia; three taels each of ginseng, jujube seed, fried yam, prepared bai zi ren (biota seed), poria, dogwood, and ophiopogon; one tael each of northern five-flavor fruit, polygala, and calamus; and three qian of cardamom. Grind all into powder and make into pills with honey, to be taken with five qian of boiling water. The effectiveness of this pill lies in its treatment for the kidneys, less so for the heart. When the heart is tranquil, the kidney energy remains stable; when the kidney energy is stable, the heart is not disturbed. Thus, treating the heart is indeed a means of treating the kidneys, and treating the kidneys is likewise a way to treat the heart.

    For heart-related ailments, such as distress and insomnia, this is due to a deficiency of heart blood. The recipe uses three qian each of ginseng, ophiopogon, poria, and angelica, two qian of red sage, and five qian each of raw and cooked jujube seeds, along with one qian each of calamus, licorice, and schisandra fruit, simmered in water for consumption. The effectiveness of this recipe lies in using five qian each of raw and cooked jujube seeds while employing nourishing heart herbs as adjuncts. The jujube seed is a supreme remedy for calming the heart and treating insomnia; the raw seed keeps one from sleeping during the day, while the cooked seed allows for peaceful nights without waking.[43p]

    日夜既安，则怔忡自定，又何必用虎睛、琥珀、丹砂之多事哉？　　怔忡之证，扰扰不宁，心神恍惚，惊悸不已，此肝肾之虚而心气之弱也。若作痰治，往往杀人。盖肾虚以致心气不交，心虚以致肝气益耗，不治虚而反攻痰，安得不速死乎？一方名宁静汤，生枣仁、麦冬、白朮各五钱，人参、白芍、熟地、元参各一两，白芥子三钱，水煎服。此方一派补心肝肾之药，三经同治，则阴阳之气自交，上下相资，怔忡自定，而惊悸恍惚之证亦尽除矣。怔忡治之不得法，多致危亡。此证乃因泄精之时，又得气恼，更不慎色而成者也。似乎宜治肾为主，不知愈补肾而心气愈加怔忡者，何故？因肝得气恼，肝气大旺，补肾则肝气更旺，反去增心之火，故愈加怔忡也。[44p]

    When day and night are at peace, then the state of anxiety settles naturally, so why resort to remedies like tiger's eye, amber, or cinnabar? The symptoms of anxiety involve disturbance and restlessness, leading to a scattered mind and continuous palpitations, which are due to deficiency of the liver and kidneys and weakness of the heart's qi. If one resorts to phlegm treatment, it often leads to severe consequences. This is because kidney deficiency prevents the heart's qi from harmonizing, and heart deficiency further depletes the liver's qi. If one treats the phlegm instead of addressing the deficiency, how could death be avoided?

    There is a formula called Tranquility Decoction, which includes five qian each of jujube seeds, ophiopogon, and white atractylodes, as well as one liang each of ginseng, white peony, cooked rehmannia, and bog bean, plus three qian of white mustard seed, all to be decocted and taken. This formula serves as a tonic for the heart, liver, and kidneys, harmonizing the three channels, allowing the yin and yang qi to interact, thereby settling the anxiety and completely alleviating the symptoms of palpitations and confusion.

    Improper treatment of anxiety can lead to severe dangers. This condition often arises from seminal leakage accompanied by emotional distress, especially if one is careless about matters of attraction. It seems sensible to treat the kidneys primarily; however, why does strengthening the kidneys lead to increased anxiety? This happens because the liver becomes agitated, with its qi becoming overly vigorous; thus, supplementing the kidneys only causes the liver's qi to thrive further, which in turn exacerbates the heart's fire, leading to increased anxiety.[44p]

    然则心不可补乎？心不补则火不能息，补心而又加去火之药则得生矣。方用化忡丹，人参、生枣仁各二钱，麦冬、白芍、元参、茯神各五钱，黄连、白芥子各一钱，甘草五分，水煎服。此方妙在不去定心，反去泻火；尤妙在不去泻肝，反去补肝；尤妙在不去补肾，反去补肺。盖泻心火，即所以定心气也，补肝气则肝平，肝平则心亦平，补肺气则肺旺，能制肝经之旺矣。制服相宜，自然心气得养，而怔忡有不全愈者乎？　　健忘，上病也。方用人参、芡实、麦冬、生枣仁、当归、山茱萸各三两，五味子、远志、菖蒲、柏子仁去油各一两，熟地五两，莲须二两，山药四两，各为末，蜜为丸，每日早晚，各用白滚水送下各五钱，半料而痊。古今图书集成医部全录卷三百二十

    However, can the heart not be replenished? If the heart is not replenished, the fire cannot be extinguished. By replenishing the heart and simultaneously using medications to clear the fire, one can achieve rejuvenation. The prescription uses Huazhong Dan, which includes two qian each of ginseng and jujube seed, five qian each of ophiopogon, white peony, original bellflower, and poria, one qian each of coptis and white mustard seed, and five fen of licorice, boiled in water for consumption. This formula is remarkable in not only calming the heart but also reducing fire; especially noteworthy is how it does not just descend liver fire but also nourishes the liver; even more remarkable is its capacity not to just replenish the kidney but also to nourish the lungs. The decrease of heart fire is exactly what calms the heart energy, and nourishing liver energy leads to a balanced liver, which in turn harmonizes the heart. Nourishing lung energy enables the lungs to thrive, thus controlling the exuberance of the liver meridian. When these methods are appropriately balanced, it naturally nourishes the heart energy, allowing for complete recovery from anxiety.

    Forgetfulness is a sign of illness. The prescription uses three liang each of ginseng, fox nut, ophiopogon, jujube seed, angelica, and cornelian cherry; one liang each of schisandra, polygala, sweet flag, and biota seed without oil; five liang of cooked rehmannia, two liang of lotus beard, and four liang of yam, all ground into powder, formed into pills with honey. Each morning and evening, take five qian with boiling water, and recovery is achieved in half the time.

    　　平补镇心丹 【《局方》】 　治心血不足，时或怔忡，夜多异梦，如堕崖谷。常服，安心肾，益荣卫。　　酸枣仁炒，二钱半　车前子　白茯苓　麦门冬　五味子　茯神　桂心不见火，各一两二钱半　龙齿　熟地黄酒蒸　天门冬　远志甘草水煮　山药姜汁制，各一两半　人参　朱砂飞，各半两　　右为末，炼蜜丸如桐子大，以前朱砂为衣，每服三十丸，空心米汤温酒任下。
    　　平补镇心丸　治前证。
    　　熟地黄　生地黄　山药　天门冬　麦门冬　柏子仁　茯神各四两，一本七两　辰砂另研为衣　桔梗各三两　远志甘草制，七两　当归四两　石菖蒲节密者，十六两　龙骨一两　　右为细末，炼蜜为丸如梧子大，每服二十丸，空心米饮吞下，温酒亦得。渐加至五十丸。宜常服。[52p]

    Ping Bu Zhen Xin Dan (Heart-Calming and Nourishing Pill)

    This formula treats insufficiency of heart blood, occasionally causing palpitations, frequent strange dreams at night, as if falling into a ravine. Regular use calms the heart, supports the kidney, and nourishes the body's protective energy.

    Ingredients:

    • Stir-fried sour jujube seeds: 2.5 qian
    • Plantago seeds: 1 liang
    • White poria: 1 liang
    • Ophiopogon: 1 liang
    • Schisandra: 1 liang
    • Poria: 1 liang
    • Cinnamon heart (not heated): 2.5 qian
    • Dragon bone: 1 liang
    • Prepared rehmannia: steamed with wine
    • Asparagus: 1.5 liang
    • Polygala: cooked with licorice: 1.5 liang
    • Chinese yam: prepared with ginger juice: 1.5 liang
    • Ginseng: 0.5 liang
    • Cinnabar: 0.5 liang

    Grind the above into a fine powder, form into pills the size of a tung seed, coat with the previously prepared cinnabar. Take thirty pills with warm rice soup or wine on an empty stomach.

    Ping Bu Zhen Xin Wan (Heart-Calming and Nourishing Pill)

    This formula treats previous conditions.

    Ingredients:

    • Prepared rehmannia: 4 liang
    • Fresh rehmannia: 4 liang
    • Chinese yam: 4 liang
    • Asparagus: 4 liang
    • Ophiopogon: 4 liang
    • Cedar nuts: 4 liang
    • Poria: 4 liang (originally 7 liang)
    • Various herbs (for coating): 3 liang
    • Polygala with licorice: 7 liang
    • Angelica: 4 liang
    • Acorus: 16 liang (dense pieces)
    • Dragon bone: 1 liang

    Grind into a fine powder, form into pills the size of a walnut, take twenty pills with warm rice drink, or warm wine is also acceptable. Gradually increase to fifty pills. Regular use is advisable.[52p]

    　　远志丸　治因事有所大惊，梦寐不祥，登高涉险，神魂不安，心志恐怯。　　远志姜汁制　石菖蒲各五钱　茯苓　茯神　人参　龙齿各一两　　右为末，炼蜜和丸如桐子大，辰砂为衣，每服七十丸，食后临卧热水下。

    Yuan Zhi Pill: Treats distress from great shock, ominous dreams, climbing high and encountering dangers, unsettled spirit, and fearful heart.
    Ingredients: Yuan Zhi, ginger juice, each five qian; Shi Chang Pu, Fu Ling, Fu Shen, Ren Shen, Long Chi, each one liang.
    Grind the above into powder, process with honey to form pills the size of tung seeds, coat with cinnabar. Take seventy pills after meals with hot water before lying down.

    Amber Nourishing Heart Pill: Treats heart blood deficiency, palpitations, restless nights, or heart fluttering.
    Ingredients: Amber, ground separately, two qian; Long Chi, calcined and ground separately, one liang; Shi Chang Pu, Yuan Zhi, black beans, and licorice cooked together after bones are removed; Fu Shen; fried sour jujube seeds; Ren Shen, each five qian; Dang Gui, raw Di Huang, each seven qian; Zhu Sha, powdered; Huang Lian, each three qian; Bai Zi Ren, five qian; Niu Huang, ground separately, one qian.
    Grind all to a fine powder, mix Niu Huang, Zhu Sha, Amber, and Long Chi until extremely fine, form into pills the size of millet grains, coat with gold leaf. Take fifty pills with lampwick tea.

    Ding Zhi Pill: Treats insufficient heart qi, palpitations, and fearfulness.
    Ingredients: Shi Chang Pu fried, Yuan Zhi, each two liang; Fu Shen, Ren Shen, each three liang.
    Grind to powder, process with honey to form pills the size of tung seeds, coat with Zhu Sha. Take fifty pills with rice soup. One variation omits Fu Shen, named Kai Xin San, take two qian at any time.[53p]

    Ningzhi Pill: Treats heart deficiency, insufficient blood, and excessive fear.

    Nourishing Heart Decoction (as per "De Xiaofang"): Treats heart deficiency, insufficient blood, and restless vigilance.
    Ingredients: Honey-fried Licorice (five fen), roasted Astragalus, Fu Shen, Bai Fu Ling, Ban Xia Qu, Dang Gui, Chuan Xiong (each seven coins and a half), Yuan Zhi with ginger juice (baked), Bai Zi Ren, Jujube Seed (aromatic after being roasted between paper), spicy cinnamon, Wuweizi, Ginseng (each one coin).     Iron Essence Pill: Treats convulsions and confusion, causing restless sleep.

    Grind into a fine powder, mix thoroughly, knead with honey to form pills the size of a Chinese parasol tree seed. Take twenty pills each time, swallowed with congee or soup, without specific timing.

    Poria Pill: Treats heart wind deficiency, palpitations, and forgetfulness.
    Ingredients: Poria, ginseng, Mai Men Dong, Scutellaria, cooked Rehmannia, biota seed, Job's tears, and rhinoceros horn, each one tael; dragon teeth powder and iron powder, each one and a half taels; Fang Feng and Astragalus, each seven and a half qian.
