    Ginseng Pill: Treats heart wind deficiency, palpitations, and anxiety, often after worry, resulting in confusion and unrest.
    Ingredients: Ginseng, cooked Rehmannia, dragon teeth (each one tael), Poria (one and a half taels), white Atractylodes, honey-baked Licorice, Ophiopogon (each half a tael), Siler (seven and a half qian), gold leaf and silver leaf (fifty pieces each).
    Process: Grind into a fine powder, mix evenly, knead with honey, and crush 200 to 300 times until shaped like a walnut. Take fifteen pills each time, no specific timing, wash down with congee.

    Poria and Licorice Decoction (Zhongjing): Treats water retention in the heart with palpitations.
    Ingredients: Poria, cinnamon twig (each three qian), fresh ginger (half a tael), Licorice (two qian).
    Process: Use two cups of water, decoct until one cup remains, take at any time.

    Poria Decoction (from "Jisheng Fang", same below): Treats phlegm and fluid retention in the heart and stomach, chronic palpitations.
    Ingredients: Red Poria, Pinellia (each one and a half qian), Poria, Ophiopogon, tangerine peel (each one and a half qian), betel nut, sandalwood (untouched by fire), honey-baked Licorice (each one qian).
    Process: Use two cups of water, three slices of ginger, decoct to eight parts, take away from meals. One version omits betel nut.

    Ginger and Atractylodes Decoction: Treats water retention and palpitations.
    Ingredients: Fresh ginger, Atractylodes, Poria, Pinellia (each one qian), spicy cinnamon, Licorice (each five fen).
    Process: Use one cup of water, three slices of ginger, one red date, decoct to six parts, take at any time.[56p]

    Zhì Gān Cǎo Tāng (Braised Licorice Decoction), also known as Fù Mài Tāng (Restoring Pulse Decoction), treats pulse knotting and alternation, as well as heart palpitations. Ingredients: Licorice 1.2 ounces, Ginseng and Ejiao (Gelatinized Donkey-hide) 0.6 ounces each, Hemp Seed, Cinnamon Twig, Ophiopogon 1 ounce each, Raw Rehmannia 1.5 ounces. Prepare with 5 sheng of water and wine each, 1 ounce of fresh ginger, 12 jujubes, 2.3 sheng of clear wine, and 2.7 sheng of water; boil down to 2 sheng, strain, then dissolve all Ejiao, and divide into three doses.

    Yì Róng Tāng (Nourishing Glory Decoction) treats excessive worrying, which depletes heart blood, leading to a state of being scattered and unfocused. Symptoms include palpitations, propensity to sadness, pale complexion, insomnia at night, and possibly cloudy urination. Ingredients: White Peony Root, Astragalus, Ginseng, small Licorice, Poria, roasted Jujube Seed, roasted Biota Seed, uncooked Wood Fragrance, Ophiopogon, and wine-soaked Angelica each 0.1 ounce; also burn and grind purple quartz. Mix with braised Licorice. For one dose, use 2 cups of water, 3 slices of ginger, and 1 jujube, stew for a time, taken as needed. One version omits Ophiopogon.

    Mì Chuán Suān Zǎo Rén Tāng (Secret Transmission Sour Jujube Seed Decoction) treats disharmony between heart and kidney, deficiency of essence and blood, the presence of phlegm, leading to palpitations, disorientation, and disturbed sleep at night. Ingredients: Roasted Jujube Seed, Prepared Polygala, Astragalus, White Poria, wine-soaked Angelica, Lotus Seed, Ginseng, and Poria each 1 ounce; dried Citrus Peel and braised Licorice each 0.5 ounce. Steep, and take 4 qian (15 grams) each time, with 1.5 cups of water, 3 slices of ginger, and 1 jujube; simmer in a clay vessel to reduce to 70%, take twice daily, with one dose before bed.[57p]

    　　叶氏镇心爽神汤　治心肾不交，上盛下虚，心神恍惚，睡多惊悸，小便频数，遗泄白浊。　　石菖蒲半两　甘草炙四钱　人参　酸枣仁炒　赤茯苓　当归酒浸焙，各三钱　南星泡　陈皮　山药　细辛　紫菀　半夏制　川芎　覆盆子　通草　麦冬　五味　柏子仁炒　枸杞各二钱半　　右(口父)咀，每服四钱，水一盏，蜜一匙，煎五分，去滓，入麝香少许，再煮一二沸，温服，不拘时。

    Ye's Tranquil Heart and Refreshing Spirit Decoction
    Treats the imbalance between heart and kidneys, with excessive upper activity and deficiency in the lower body, leading to a wandering spirit, excessive sleep with anxiety, frequent urination, and white, turbid leakage.

    • Half a tael of Acorus calamus
    • Four qian of honey-fried licorice
    • Three qian each of ginseng, fried sour jujube seed, red poria, and wine-immersed angelica
    • Three qian each of nux vomica, dried tangerine peel, Chinese yam, fine gentian, purple aster, processed pinellia, chuanxiong, raspberry, hemp seed, lily, and five-flavor fruit
    • Two and a half qian each of fried biota seed and goji berry

    Take four qian of the above, with one cup of water and one spoonful of honey, decoct for five minutes, strain, add a small amount of musk, and boil for another minute or two. Take warm, not restricted to time.

    Selected Unique Formula by Scholar Yu
    Treats persistent anxiety, forgetting the past and losing focus.

    • Twelve fen each of sandalwood, white poria, and cassia seed
    • Four fen each of Acorus calamus, borneo camphor, cooked rehmannia, suhexiang, and rhinoceros horn
    • Six fen each of asparagus, polygala, and ginseng
    • Ten fen of licorice

    Grind to a fine powder, refine with honey into pills the size of cherries. Take one pill after meals, dissolve in the mouth, or swallow with rice drink.

    Ginseng Milk Pill
    Treats deficiency of heart qi, palpitations, and spontaneous sweating.

    • One tael of ginseng
    • Three qian of frankincense, ground separately
    • Two taels of angelica

    Grind all to a fine powder and mix, then cook Chinese yam into a paste, form pills the size of phoenix seeds. Take thirty pills after meals, swallowed with jujube soup.[58p]

    　　龙齿丹　治心血虚寒，怔仲不已，痰多恍惚。　　当归酒浸　龙齿　远志甘草水煮　枣仁炒研　官桂　琥珀　附子炮去皮脐，切作八片，姜汁浸　南星銼碎，姜汁浸一宿，各一两　木香　沉香　紫石英煅酢淬　熟地黄酒蒸焙，各半两　　右为细末，炼蜜和丸如梧桐子大，朱砂为衣，每服五十丸，不拘时，用枣汤送下。
    　　灵砂宁志丸　治男妇大病后，损伤荣卫失血过多，精血虚损，心神恍惚，不得眠睡，饮食全减，肌体瘦弱。　　辰砂二两，不夹石者，夹绢袋盛，悬于银石器内，用椒红三两，取井华水调椒入于器内，可八分，别用锅子注水，置朱砂器在内，重汤煮令鱼眼沸，三昼夜为度，取出辰砂水飞细　茯神　鹿茸燎去毛酥炙黄　黄芪蜜炙　白朮　人参各三两　石菖蒲二两　　右为末，入辰砂研匀，枣肉和杵一二千下，丸如梧桐子大，每服三十丸，空心，温酒米饮任下。[59p]

    Dragon Tooth Pill: Treats heart and blood deficiency with cold symptoms, persistent shock, and excessive phlegm leading to confusion.     Heart Elixir: It treats both men and women with insufficient heart energy and unsettled spirits, addressing all heart-related ailments.

    Ingredients:

    • 50 taels of cinnabar
    • Sweet and bitter herbs boiled together
    • Ginseng
    • Fried bitter gourd seeds
    • Steamed and roasted prepared cooked rehmannia
    • Stone calamus
    • Roasted angelica
    • Ophiopogon
    • Astragalus
    • Fried stone lotus flesh
    • Polygala root
    • Tuckahoe
    • Each of the above three taels
    • 5 taels of atractylodes

    Preparation method:
    Combine the fourteen ingredients, grind, and mix thoroughly. Then take the cinnabar and mix it while hot, storing it in a silk bag tightly sewn shut with hemp thread. Use a clay pot, placing a weighted silver container inside. Add 20 pounds of white honey and hang the medicine bag in the center, ensuring it does not touch the bottom, allowing the honey to soak the bag. Use mulberry wood to keep it boiling continuously for three days until the honey turns dark and black. Replace the honey and cook for another seven days, then stop the fire and remove the concoction, discarding the herbs and cleaning the cinnabar until dry. Place it inside beef heart and steam again in the silver container. If the broth gets low, add hot water from the side of the pot. Continue steaming until the heart is soft, then replace the cinnabar and repeat the steaming process for a total of seven times. Once the cinnabar is cooked, rinse it in boiling water until clean and dry it. Grind it in a mortar until it is very fine, then form balls the size of peas using glutinous rice paste. Let them dry in the shade. The dosage is twenty balls, taken after meals with ginseng soup, jujube soup, or ophiopogon soup as preferred.[61p]

    Zao Ren Decoction is used to treat great weakness and exhaustion, dreams of seminal emission, weakness in the body, depletion of blood and energy, and conditions caused by drunkenness or overindulgence in physical relations. Symptoms include anxiety, restlessness, and urgency in the lower abdomen.

    Ingredients: two taels of Zao Ren, one tael each of Ze Xia, Ren Shen, Shao Yao, Gui Xin; two taels each of Huang Qi, Gan Cao, Fu Ling, Bai Long Gu, and Mu Li; three slices of Sheng Jiang and one he of Ban Xia.

    Combine the twelve ingredients, grind together, and boil with nine sheng of water until four sheng remain. Take seven he at a time, three times a day. If unable to eat due to urgency in the lower abdomen, add six taels of Gui Xin.

    Xiao Jian Zhong Decoction treats heart palpitations due to deficiency, dryness of the throat, dry lips, and a pale complexion. It may also alleviate loss of taste in food and weakness of yin and yang. Symptoms include sadness, lethargy, prolonged lying down, prolonged cases lasting years or lighter cases lasting a hundred days, leading to gradual thinness and depletion of the five organs’ energy, making recovery difficult.

    Ingredients: two taels of Gan Cao, three taels each of Gui Xin and Sheng Jiang, six taels of Shao Yao, one sheng of Jiao Yi, and twelve dates.

    Combine these six ingredients, grind together, and boil with nine sheng of water until three sheng remain. Remove the sediment and mix in the Jiao Yi. Take one sheng at a time, three times a day, and after three days, repeat making a dose, after which it can be combined with various pills and powders.[67p]

    　　茯神汤，治五邪气入人体中，见鬼妄语，有所见闻，心悸跳动，恍惚不定。　　茯神去木　人参　石菖蒲　白茯苓各三两　赤小豆四十枚　　右五味(口父)咀，以水一斗，煮取二升半，分三服。
    　　归脾汤　治思虑过多，劳心伤脾，健忘怔忡，烦躁不寐，短气自汗，坐卧不安。　　木香四分　人参　茯神　黄芪　远志　白朮　当归身各一钱　龙眼肉十个　炙甘草五分　枣仁八分，研　　右，水二锺，姜三片，枣二枚，煎八分，不拘时服。
    　　朱雀丸　惊悸怔忡，此方主之。
    　　白茯苓二两　沉香五钱
    　　二味为丸。

    　　加减二陈汤　心若时跳时止，是痰因火动。　　陈皮　半夏　茯苓　甘草　枳实　麦门冬　竹茹　炒黄连　炒山栀　人参　白朮　当归　辰砂　乌梅　竹沥　　右，姜三片，枣一枚，水煎，调辰砂末服。[68p]

    Fuzheng Decoction treats the intrusion of five evil Qi into the human body, leading to hallucinations, anxiety, heart palpitations, and a disturbed state of mind. Ingredients include three liang each of Fu Shen (Poria), Ginseng, Shi Chang Pu (Acori Tatarinowii), and Bai Fu Ling (White Poria), and forty pieces of red adzuki beans. The five ingredients should be chewed, boiled in ten dou of water, and reduced to two and a half sheng to be divided into three doses.

    Gui Pi Decoction addresses excessive thinking, heart strain, spleen damage, forgetfulness, anxiety leading to insomnia, shortness of breath with sweating, and restlessness. It contains four fen of Mu Xiang, one qian each of Ginseng, Fu Shen, Huang Qi (Astragalus), Yuan Zhi (Polygala), Bai Zhu (Atractylodes), and Dang Gui, ten pieces of longan meat, five fen of roasted licorice, and eight fen of jujube seeds, crushed. Boil the mixture with two zhong of water, three slices of ginger, and two jujubes until reduced to eight parts, taken at any time.

    Zhuque Pill treats anxiety and restlessness. It consists of two liang of Bai Fu Ling and five qian of Chen Xiang (Agarwood), combined into pills.

    Jia Jian Er Chen Decoction is for a heart that beats erratically, indicating phlegm stimulated by heat. Ingredients include Chen Pi (dried tangerine peel), Ban Xia (Pinellia), Fu Ling, Gan Cao (licorice), Zhi Shi (bitter orange), Mai Men Dong (Ophiopogon), Zhu Ru (bamboo shavings), fried Huang Lian (Coptis), fried Shan Zhi (gardenia), Ginseng, Bai Zhu, Dang Gui, Chen Sha (cinnabar), Wu Mei (black plum), and Zhu Li (bamboo juice). Boil with three slices of ginger and one jujube, then adjust with powdered cinnabar for consumption.[68p]

    　　养血宁心汤
    　　当归一钱二分　白芍药酒炒　栀子七分　黄芩　黄连各八分　枣仁　生地各一钱　远志　麦冬各二钱　　姜枣煎服。

    　　寿星丸 【《济生方》，下同】 　治因病惊忧，涎留心胞，精神不守，谵言妄语，不得安卧。　　生天南星一斤　琥珀一两，别研　朱砂飞二两　　右为细末和匀，用生姜自然汁，打面糊为丸如菉豆大，每服四十丸，不拘时候，用人参石菖蒲煎汤送下淡姜汤亦得。若心气狂甚，入铁艳粉一两。
    　　远志饮子　治心劳虚寒，惊悸恍惚，多忘不安，梦寐惊魇。　　远志甘草煮　茯苓　桂心　人参　枣仁炒　黄芪　当归酒浸，各一两　甘草炙，半两　　右(口父)咀，每服四钱，水一盏半，姜五片，煎至七分，去滓温服，不拘时候。[69p]

    Nourishing Blood and Calming the Heart Decoction

    Ingredients:

    • 1.2 qian of Angelica (Dang Gui)
    • 0.7 qian of fried White Peony Root (Bai Shao Yao) in wine
    • 0.7 qian of Gardenia (Zhi Zi)
    • 0.8 qian each of Scutellaria (Huang Qin) and Coptis (Huang Lian)
    • 1 qian each of Jujube Seed (Zao Ren) and Raw Rehmannia (Sheng Di)
    • 2 qian each of Polygala (Yuan Zhi) and Ophiopogon (Mai Dong)

    Preparation: Boil with ginger and jujubes for consumption.

    Shou Xing Pills (from "Ji Sheng Fang")

    Indication: For conditions caused by illness leading to shock and worry, phlegm accumulation in the heart, mental disturbances, nonsensical speech, and difficulty sleeping.

    Ingredients:

    • 1 jin of fresh Tian Nan Xing ( rhizome of the plant)
    • 1 liang of Amber (Hu Po), ground separately
    • 2 liang of Cinnabar (Zhu Sha)

    Preparation: Grind into a fine powder, mix with fresh ginger juice to form pills the size of soybeans. Take 40 pills at a time without restriction on timing. Can also be taken with broth made from ginseng and Acorus (Shi Chang Pu) or diluted ginger soup. If there are severe heart disturbances, add 1 liang of iron powder.

    Yuan Zhi Decoction

    Indication: For heart labor, deficiency, coldness, agitation, forgetfulness, and nightmares.

    Ingredients:

    • 1 liang each of Polygala (Yuan Zhi), Licorice (Gan Cao), Poria (Fu Ling), cinnamon heart (Gui Xin), Ginseng (Ren Shen), and fried Jujube Seed (Zao Ren)
    • 1 liang of Astragalus (Huang Qi)
    • 1 liang of Angelica (Dang Gui) soaked in wine
    • 0.5 liang of roasted Licorice

    Preparation: Chew the above ingredients. Take 4 qian with 1.5 cups of water and 5 slices of ginger, boil down to 70%. Strain and take warm, without restriction on timing.[69p]

    　　茯神汤　治脉虚极，咳则心痛，喉中介介如梗状，甚则咽肿，惊悸不安。　　茯神　人参　远志　甘草煮　通草　麦门冬　黄芪　桔梗銼炒　甘草炙，各等分　　右(口父)咀，每服四钱，水一盏半，姜五片，煎至七分，去滓温服，不拘时候。
    　　大建中汤　治诸虚不足，小腹急痛，胁肋(月真)胀，骨肉酸痛，短气喘逆，痰多咳嗽，潮热多汗，心下惊悸，腰背强痛，多卧少起。　　黄芪蜜炙　附子炮去皮脐　鹿茸酒蒸　续断　地骨皮　白芍药　石斛　人参　当归酒浸　川芎　小草各一两　甘草炙，半两　　右(口父)咀，每服四钱，水一盏半，生姜五片，煎至七分，去滓温服，不拘时候。
    　　心肾丸　治心肾不足，精少血燥，心下烦热，怔忡不安，或口干生疮，目赤头运，小便赤浊，五心烦热，多渴引饮。但是精虚血少，不受峻补者，悉宜服之。　　菟丝子淘酒蒸擂　麦门冬各二两[70p]

    Fried Shen Decoction: Treats extreme deficiency of the pulse, with cough causing heart pain, a sensation in the throat like a lump, and in severe cases, throat swelling, fear, and restlessness.

    Ingredients: Fu Shen, Ren Shen, Yuan Zhi, Gan Cao (cooked), Tong Cao, Mai Men Dong, Huang Qi, Jie Geng (dry-fried), Gan Cao (roasted), all equal parts.

    Preparation: Chew the right ingredients, take four qian per dose, boil with one and a half bowls of water and five slices of ginger until reduced to three-quarters, strain and take warm, without time restriction.

    Great Jian Zhong Decoction: Treats various deficiencies, urgency and pain in the lower abdomen, distension in the sides, soreness in the bones and muscles, shortness of breath with wheezing, excessive phlegm and cough, tidal fever and profuse sweating, palpitations of the heart, and stiffness in the waist and back, with a tendency to lie down and not rise much.

    Ingredients: Honey-fried Huang Qi, prepared Fu Zi (skins and umbilicus removed), deer antler (steamed in wine), Xu Duan, Di Gu Pi, Bai Shao Yao, Shi Hu, Ren Shen, Dang Gui (soaked in wine), Chuan Xiong, Xiao Cao (each one tael), and roasted Gan Cao (half a tael).

    Preparation: Chew the right ingredients, take four qian per dose, boil with one and a half bowls of water and five slices of fresh ginger until reduced to three-quarters, strain and take warm, without time restriction.

    Heart-Kidney Pills: Treats deficiency of the heart and kidneys, diminished essence and dry blood, irritability and heat in the heart, restlessness, possible dry mouth with sores, red eyes and head dizziness, turbid red urine, five hearts hot and restless, excessive thirst leading to drinking.

    This is suitable for those with essence deficiency and low blood who cannot tolerate harsh tonics.

    Ingredients: Tu Si Zi (washed, steamed, and pounded), Mai Men Dong (each two taels).[70p]

    　　右为细末，炼蜜为丸如梧桐子大，每服七十丸，空心食前，用盐汤送下，熟水亦得。
    　　茸朱丹　治心虚血少，神志不宁，惊惕恍惚，夜多异梦，睡卧不安。　　鹿茸去毛酒蒸，一两　朱砂半两，水飞，蜜炒尤佳　　右为细末，煮枣肉为丸如梧桐子大，每服四十丸，炒酸枣仁煎汤送下，午前临卧服之。
    　　茸附汤　治精血俱虚，荣卫耗损，潮热自汗，怔忡惊悸，肢体倦乏，但是一切虚弱之证，皆宜服之。　　鹿茸去毛酒蒸　附子炮去皮脐，各一两　　右(口父)咀，分作四服，水二盏，生姜十片，煎至八分，去滓，食前温服。
    　　二白丸 【《元戎》】 　治痰涎为病患，以致癫癎狂妄惊悸等证。　　白矾一两　轻粉一字或半钱，量虚实加减　　右用生蒸饼剂裹，蒸熟去皮，可丸，入轻粉，丸如梧桐子大，每服二三十丸，生姜汤下。小儿服如黍米大。[71p]

    The above is a detailed prescription for various medicinal formulations used in traditional Chinese medicine. Here’s the translation:

    The right side is a fine powder. Refine honey into pills the size of a phoenix tree seed. Take seventy pills at a time, on an empty stomach before meals, with salty broth or warm water.

    Rong Zhu Dan: Used to treat heart deficiency, sparse blood, unsettled spirit, fear and confusion, frequent strange dreams at night, and restless sleep.

    Deer antler, hair removed, steamed in wine, one tael; Cinnabar, half a tael; water-fly powder, honey fried is best. The right side is a fine powder, boil jujube flesh to form pills the size of a phoenix tree seed. Take forty pills at a time, with decoction of fried sour jujube seeds before noon.

    Rong Fu Tang: Used to treat deficiency of essence and blood, depletion of nutritive and defensive qi, tidal fever with spontaneous sweating, palpitations and fear, fatigue in limbs. It is suitable for all symptoms of deficiency.

    Deer antler, hair removed, steamed in wine; Aconite, processed and peeled, both one tael. The right (mouth father) to chew, divided into four doses, with two cups of water, ten slices of fresh ginger, decoct to eight portions, strain, and take warm before meals.

    Er Bai Wan: Treatment for phlegm and mucus-related diseases that lead to symptoms such as seizures, mania, and palpitations.

    Alum, one tael; light powder, a character or half a qian, adjust quantity according to deficiency or surplus. The right side is to wrap with fresh steamed pancake, steam until cooked, remove the skin, can be formed into pills, add light powder, and roll into pills the size of a phoenix tree seed. Take twenty to thirty pills at a time, with ginger broth. For children, use the size of millet.[71p]

    　　朱砂安神丸　治心神烦乱，怔忡不安，兀兀欲吐，胸中气乱而有热，若懊憹之状，皆膈上血中伏火，蒸蒸而不安，宜从权衡法，以镇阴火之浮行，以养上焦之元气。　　朱砂另研，水飞阴干　黄连各一钱　生地三分　当归　炙甘草各半钱　　右为末，酒浸蒸饼丸如黍米大，朱砂为衣，每服十五丸，津唾送下，食后。此缓治之理也。
    　　黄连安神丸　外物卒惊，宜此以镇之。　　朱砂细研水飞　生地黄　当归头各一钱　黄连酒炒，一钱五分　甘草炙，五分　　右为极细末，蒸饼丸黄豆大，每服十丸，津下。
    　　控涎丹　治惊则神出于舍，舍空涎入。　　甘遂去心　紫大戟去皮　白芥子各等分　　右为末，煮糊丸桐子大，临卧，淡姜汤下七丸。[72p]

    Zhu Sha An Shen Wan: Treats disturbances of the mind, anxiety, restlessness, a sensation of nausea, chaotic and heated qi in the chest, resembling frustration. These symptoms indicate stagnant blood and hidden fire in the diaphragm, causing agitation. It is advisable to use balancing methods to calm the floating yin fire and nourish the original qi of the upper pathway.

    Ingredients: Zhu Sha (red mercury) ground and dried with water, Huang Lian (coptis) each 1 qian, Sheng Di (raw rehmannia) 3 fen, Dang Gui (angelica) and Zhi Gan Cao (prepared licorice) each 0.5 qian.

    Preparation: Grind the above into a powder, soak in wine, and form into pills the size of millet grains, coated with Zhu Sha. Dosage: take fifteen pills, swallowed with saliva, after meals. This is a method of gentle treatment.

    Huang Lian An Shen Wan: For sudden fright, this helps to calm it down.

    Ingredients: Zhu Sha finely ground and dried with water, Sheng Di Huang (raw rehmannia) and Dang Gui (angelica) each 1 qian; Huang Lian (coptis) roasted with wine, 1.5 qian; Zhi Gan Cao (prepared licorice) 0.5 qian.

    Preparation: Grind everything into an extremely fine powder, form into pills the size of soybeans, and take ten pills with saliva.

    Kong Yan Dan: Treats situations where fright causes the spirit to leave the body, and the body's essence fills with saliva.

    Ingredients: Gan Sui (periploca) to clear the heart, Zi Da Ji (purple skinned euphorbia) peeled, Bai Jie Zi (white mustard seed) each equal portions.

    Preparation: Grind into a powder, form it into pills the size of tung seeds, and take seven pills with light ginger soup before bed.[72p]

    　　羌活胜湿汤　治卧而多惊，邪在少阳厥阴。　　羌活　独活　槁本　防风各一钱　川芎二分　蔓荆子三钱　甘草炙，五分　　水二锺，煎一锺，食后服。

    Qiang Huo Sheng Shi Decoction
    Treats cases of waking in shock, with pathogens in the Shaoyang and Jueyin.
    Ingredients: Qiang Huo, Du Huo, Gao Ben, Fang Feng each 3 grams; Chuan Xiong 1 gram; Man Jing Zi 9 grams; Honey-fried Gan Cao 2.5 grams.
    Add 2 cups of water, boil down to 1 cup, and take after meals.

    Ban Xia Ma Huang Pill
    Treats palpitations under the heart.
    Ingredients: Ban Xia and Ma Huang in equal parts.
    Grind the two ingredients into a fine powder, mix with honey to form pills the size of a soybean. Take 3 pills, three times a day.

    Fu Ling Pill
    Treats shock and palpitations.
    Ingredients: Shi Chang Pu, Chen Sha, Ren Shen, Yuan Zhi, Fu Ling, Zhen Tie Fen, Fu Shen, Nvxing, and Ban Xia Qu in equal parts.
    Grind into a fine powder, use 200 grams of fresh ginger to extract juice, mix with water and cook to form pills the size of a tung seed. Use the powder to coat them, taking 10 to 20 pills with ginger soup at night.

    Gui Zhi Shu Qie Mu Li Long Gu Jiu Niang Decoction (same for Zhongjing)
    Treats complications of cold damage with yang depletion, causing restlessness and shock when rising or lying down.
    Ingredients: Gui Zhi, fresh ginger (sliced), Shu Qie each 150 grams; Honey-fried Gan Cao 100 grams; fried Mu Li 250 grams; Long Gu 200 grams; 12 large dates.
    Crush together, take 15 grams each time, with 1.5 cups of water, boil down to 80%, strain and take warm.[73p]

    　　桂枝甘草汤　洽发汗后，叉手冒心，心下悸欲得按者。　　桂枝四钱　甘草二钱
    　　右二味，以水一盏半，煎八分，去渣温服。
    　　茯苓桂枝甘草大枣汤　治发汗后，脐下悸，欲作奔豚。　　茯苓八钱　甘草炙，二钱　桂枝四钱　大枣二枚　　右作二服，以甘烂水二锺，先煮茯苓，减二分，纳诸药，煮取一盏，去滓温服，日三。作甘烂水法：取水一斗许，置大盆中，以杓扬之，水上有珠子五六千颗相逐，取用之。
    　　镇心丹 【《千金方》，下同】 　治惊悸。　　辰砂用黄松节酒浸　龙齿用远志苗酢煮　　右，只取辰砂、龙齿各等分为末，猪心血为丸如芡实大，每服一丸，以麦门冬叶、菉豆、灯心、白蜜水煎，豆熟为度，临卧咽下。小儿磨化半丸，量岁数与之。[74p]

    Gui Zhi Gan Cao Decoction: For after sweating, there is a sensation of coldness in the heart, and a fluttering sensation that feels like it needs to be pressed.

    • Ingredients: 4 qian of cinnamon twig, 2 qian of licorice.
    • Prepare the two ingredients with 1.5 cups of water, simmer until reduced to 8 parts, strain, and take warm.

    Fu Ling Gui Zhi Gan Cao Da Zao Decoction: Treats palpitations below the navel after sweating, with a sensation like a rushing upwards.

    • Ingredients: 8 qian of poria, 2 qian of honey-fried licorice, 4 qian of cinnamon twig, 2 large dates.
    • Prepare two doses with 2 bowls of sweetened water. First, boil the poria, reduce by 2 parts, then add the other herbs and boil to obtain 1 cup, strain, and take warm, three times a day. Method for sweetened water: Take about 10 liters of water, place in a large basin, and scoop it up, making beads form on the surface, then use it.

    Zhen Xin Dan: Treats palpitations.

    • Cinnabar is soaked in yellow pine resin wine; dragon's teeth are boiled with the essence of plantain.
    • Mix equal parts of cinnabar and dragon's teeth into a powder, and use pig heart's blood to form pills the size of fox nuts. Take one pill each time, prepared with the leaves of sweet potato, red bean, lantern heart, boiled with white honey water until the beans are tender, and swallow before bedtime. For children, grind half a pill, and adjust according to their age.[74p]

    　　犀角汤　治伤寒后伏热在心，怔忪惊悸，不得眠睡。　　犀角屑　山栀各半两　茵陈蒿七钱半　茯苓　芍药　生地焙，各二两　麦门冬两半　　右(口父)咀，每服五钱，水一盏半，姜二片，竹叶三七片，同煎，食后服。

    　　右，先将腰子用水二碗，煎至一碗半，细切，入二味药，同煎至八分，吃腰子，以药汁送下。有吃不尽腰子，同上二味药渣，焙干为细末，山药糊为丸梧子大，每服三五十丸，米汤下。[75p]

    Rhinoceros Horn Decoction: This treats the residual heat in the heart after typhoid, leading to confusion and palpitations, causing insomnia. Use half a tael of rhinoceros horn shavings and half a tael of mountain gardenia, along with seven and a half qian of yinchenhao, two taels each of poria, peony, and roasted raw earth, and one and a half taels of ophiopogon. Prepare by grinding these ingredients, taking five qian per dose, with a cup and a half of water, two slices of ginger, and seven to ten bamboo leaves, and decoct together, to be taken after meals.

    Calming the Spirit and Nourishing the Heart Decoction: This treats palpitations and confusion due to heart deficiency. Use twelve fen each of angelica, raw rehmannia, poria, and scutellaria, seven fen of chuanxiong, ten fen each of roasted white peony and white atractylodes, eight fen each of roasted jujube kernel and water-soaked fernroot, two qian of ophiopogon, five fen of rhizome of deep-rooted marsh plant, and three fen of licorice. Alternatively, remove fernroot, ophiopogon, scutellaria, and deep-rooted marsh plant, and add dried tangerine peel, arborvitae seeds, and wine-roasted coptis, then decoct as a dose.

    Ginseng and Angelica Kidney Decoction: This treats heart qi confusion with spontaneous sweating, and can be cured with just one or two doses. Use five qian each of ginseng and angelica, and one pig kidney. First, boil the kidney in two bowls of water until reduced to one and a half bowls, finely chop it, then add the two herbs and decoct until reduced to eight parts. Eat the kidney and drink the medicinal broth. If there is leftover kidney, dry the herbal residue and grind it into a fine powder, then make into pills the size of a wolfberry, taking thirty to fifty pills with rice soup.[75p]

    Clever Soup [from Compendium of Benevolence]

    For those who are forgetful and have difficulty remembering:

    White Poria, roots of the astragalus, licorice, boiled in water; one inch of stone calamus, nine sections, each three taels. After preparation, grind them into a fine powder. Take three to five qian each day, decocted and taken on an empty stomach after meals. Take it for a day, eight to nine times, or even more than ten times. After a long time of use, one can recite a thousand words daily.

    Kong Sheng's Pillow Recipe - for treating forgetfulness.

    Tortoise shell, dragon bone, astragalus, and calamus—equal parts, sifted fine. Take with wine, one spoonful daily, three times. Regular use enhances wisdom. According to another version, take after meals with water.

    Poria Pills - for frequent forgetfulness, preventing forgetfulness.

    Two parts of stone calamus, five parts each of poria, white poria, and ginseng; seven parts of astragalus. Prepare these five ingredients, sift them fine, take one spoonful with wine, twice a day and once at night. After five days, one will notice improvements in spirit.

    Another recipe for previous symptoms:

    Two parts of epimedium and rehmannia, three parts each of astragalus, calamus, and poria. Prepare these five ingredients, sift them fine, take one spoonful with wine, three times a day. One will not forget even in old age.

    Eight Ingredients Powder - for previous symptoms.

    Six parts of winter melon, one tael each of cinnamon, and poria; four parts of dried rehmannia; three parts each of five-flavored fruit, calamus, astragalus, and stone spurge. Prepare these eight ingredients, sift them fine, take one spoonful after meals, either with wine or water. After thirty days, strength is doubled; after sixty days, vigor is strong, and willpower is sufficient.[78p]

    Cistanche Powder: Take for a long time and you won't forget in old age.
    Two and a half qian of Cistanche wine-soaked, two and a half qian of Dipsacus, seven and a half qian each of Polygala, Acorus, and White Poria. Grind into a fine powder. Take two qian each time, mixed with warm wine after meals. In spring, take as prescribed; in summer, add five fen of Rehmannia, three fen of Scutellaria, and four fen of Ophiopogon. If it’s cold, omit these and add three fen each of Dried Ginger, Cinnamon, and Sichuan Pepper. If neither hot nor cold, no need to adjust, just take it as is. After three doses, you will find that all affairs will be well. Be cautious with strong vinegar, garlic, and raw fish; don't be careless about anything else. Slightly increase to thirty pills, do not exceed, always use this as a standard.

    　　加味定志丸　治肥人痰迷心膈，寻常怔忡。　　远志　人参　琥珀　天花粉　郁金各一两　茯苓三两　菖蒲二两　贝母　(艹舌)蒌　　右为末，姜汁竹沥丸菉豆大，每服二钱，朱砂为衣。火盛者，加炒黄连一两。
    　　朱砂消痰饮 【《医统》，下同】 　治心气痰迷心窍惊悸。　　牛胆南星半两　朱砂减半，另研　麝香二分，另研　　右为末，临卧姜汁汤调服一钱。[82p]

    Phlegm-Resolving Decoction: Treats excessive phlegm and forgetfulness. Wash Banxia seven times, four taels of Nanshing (processed), Juhong, Chifenling, and Zhishi (stir-fried), each one tael, and half a tael of honey-fried Licorice. Take four qian of the mixture, boiled in one cup of water with ten slices of ginger, reduced to eight parts; take after meals.

    Ruizhu Pill: Treats heart ailments. One pig heart, extract blood; one spoon of indigo; one tael of cinnabar for the coating. First, dry the indigo in the sun, then mix it with the pig heart blood and grind it to a pulp; finally, add powdered cinnabar to form pills the size of a phoenix tree seed. Take twenty pills at any time, washed down with tea or wine.

    Modified Tranquil Pill: Treats phlegm obstructing the heart in overweight individuals, causing common palpitations. One tael each of Yuan Zhi, Ginseng, Amber, Tianhua Fen, and Yujin; three taels of Poria; two taels of Acorus; Bai Mu (Fritillaria); grind into powder. Form into pills the size of a mung bean, using ginger juice and bamboo sap, with cinnabar for coating. For those with excess heat, add one tael of stir-fried Huanglian.

    Cinnabar Phlegm-Resolving Drink: Treats phlegm obstructing the heart meridian, causing fright and palpitations. Half a tael of Nanshing and half a tael of cinnabar (ground separately), two fen of musk, ground separately. Mix into powder and take one qian in ginger juice soup before lying down.[82p]

    宁 Zhi Gao: A remedy for loss of spirit due to shock.
    Ingredients:

    • Ginseng, processed sour jujube seeds, skin removed and stir-fried between paper
    • Mercury (cinnabar), each half tael
    • One qian of resin incense, ground finely

    Prepare the powder from the above, and blend with honey to form pills the size of a marble. Take one pill with peppermint tea.

    Ping Jing Tong Sheng San: A remedy for all types of shock, palpitations, forgetfulness, and related symptoms.
    Ingredients:

    • Angelica, ginseng, Coptis, Poria, polygala, and honey-fried licorice, each three qian
    • Acorus calamus and cinnabar, ground separately, each two qian

    Prepare fine powder from the above. Brew the powder with bamboo leaves for a decoction of two qian, and take after meals before bed.

    Suan Zao Ren Tang: A remedy for palpitations and insomnia.
    Ingredients:

    • Two sheng of sour jujube seeds
    • Two liang each of Poria, white atractylodes, ginseng, and honey-fried licorice
    • Six liang of fresh ginger
    • Eight sheng of water, boiled down to three sheng for separate doses.

    Yu Zhi Zi Wan: A remedy for insufficient heart qi, mental confusion, distorted speech, palpitations, depression, sorrowfulness, excessive emotional fluctuations, forgetfulness, insomnia, frequent strange dreams, shock upon sleeping, or occasional madness.
    Ingredients:

    • Yu Zhi Zi (prepared), white Poria, goji berries, acorus calamus, Poria, cedar seeds, ginseng, earth skin, polygala, Chinese yam, and steamed rehmannia, all in equal parts,
    • Cinnabar processed with water

    Prepare fine powder from the above. Blend with honey to form pills the size of a water chestnut. Chew one pill and take with ginseng tea.[83p]

    Happy Mind Formula
    To replenish the heart's essence and cure forgetfulness, making one sharp in hearing and sight, take on a day of the Earth (Wu Zi).

    • 1 part Calamus
    • 1 part Polygala

    Crush these into a fine powder and take a size of a thumb in spoonful after meals, which sharpens hearing and vision, allowing one to perceive matters from a distance of a thousand li, promoting longevity and expelling three hundred viruses which cannot harm.

    Top Scholar Pill
    For curing forgetfulness, opening the mind, calming the spirit, and enhancing memory:

    • 1 inch Hairless Calamus (preferably the nine-joint type)
    • 1 tael of Earth Dragon Skin
    • 1 tael of White Poria
    • 1 tael of Polygala
    • 1 tael of Licorice (soaked in water)
    • 3 qian of Ginseng
    • 5 qian of Morinda

    Grind these into powder, using 2 taels of White Poria powder and 2 taels of sticky rice, mix well. For external use, take 3 qian of Hairless Calamus, crush it, and boil it with water to make a strong decoction, strain out the residue, and form into pills. Take 35 pills after meals and at noon when lying down.

    Additionally: For treating forgetfulness. Long-term use enhances intelligence and sharpens the mind.[84p]

    Xiaoyao Drink: For women suffering from excessive thoughts and melancholy, leading to heart and spleen disturbances, with declining blood and qi, gradually resulting in irregular meridians and possibly symptoms of palpitations and anxiety. Ingredients: 2-3 qian of Angelica, 1.5 qian of White Peony, 1.5 qian of Poria, 3-5 qian of Rehmannia, 2 qian of fried Jujube Seed, 3-5 fen of prepared Polygala, 8 fen of dried Tangerine Peel, 1 qian of roasted Licorice.     Daying Decoction: For deficiencies in true yin, essence, and blood, symptoms such as palpitations and anxiety. Ingredients: 2-3 qian or 5 qian of Angelica, 3-5-7 qian of Rehmannia, 2 qian each of Goji Berries and sautéed Eucommia (silk removed), 1.5 qian of Achyranthes, 1-2 qian each of roasted Licorice and Cinnamon. Use 2 sheng of water, decoct to 7 parts, take warm on an empty stomach.

    Modified Yiyin Decoction: Generally for kidney water true yin deficiency, with many yang signs, false fire causing heat, palpitations, and anxiety, this formula is recommended. Ingredients: 2 qian each of Raw Rehmannia, Peony, and Ophiopogon, 3-5 qian of Rehmannia, 5-7 fen of roasted Licorice, 1 qian each of Anemarrhena and Lycium Bark. Use 2 sheng of water, decoct and consume.

    Yin Regulation Decoction: For deficiencies in spleen and kidney, with symptoms such as palpitations and anxiety, a warming and moistening approach is recommended. Ingredients: 3-5-7 qian or 1-2 liang of Rehmannia, 1-2 qian of roasted Licorice, 2-3 qian or 5-7 qian of Angelica, 1-2-3 qian of dry Ginger (yellow fried). Use 2 sheng of water, decoct to 7-8 parts hot for consumption. Optionally, add 1-2 qian of Cinnamon.[88p]

    　　　　单方

    　　九窍出血，因暴惊而得，其脉虚者：灵砂三十粒，人参汤下，三服愈。此证不可错认作血得气则流，妄用凉药误事。【《直指方》】
    　　急惊昏迷，不省人事：石绿四两，轻粉一钱为末，薄荷汁入酒，调一字服，取吐。
    　　怔忡自汗，心气不足也：用獖猪腰子二个，以水二碗，煮至一碗半，细切，人参、当归各半两，同煎至八分，空心吃腰子，以汁送下。其渣焙干为末，以山药末作糊，丸如菉豆大，每服五十丸，食远枣汤下，不过两服即愈。此昆山神济大师方也。一加乳香二钱。【《百一》】
    　　惊悸遗精：木馒头炒、白牵牛等分为末，每服二钱，用米饮调下。 【《乾坤秘韫》】
    　　心虚惊悸不定：荆沥二升，缓火煎取一升六合，分温每服四合，日三夜一。 【《千金》】
    　　蜜陀僧一物煎汤，每服匙许。惊气入心，喑不能语者，此方主之。或为末，茶调服一匕。【《身经图考》】[89p]

    Single Prescriptions

    For bleeding from the nine orifices caused by sudden fright and with a weak pulse: take thirty grains of Ling Sha and administer it with Ren Shen Decoction; three doses will cure. This symptom must not be mistaken for blood flow due to energy, as using cooling medicines wrongly can lead to mistakes.

    For sudden fright causing coma and loss of consciousness: take four ounces of Shi Lu and one penny weight of Qing Fen, grind into powder, mix with mint juice in wine, and take a dose to induce vomiting.

    For fright manifested as spontaneous sweating and insufficient heart energy: use two wild boar kidneys, add two bowls of water, and boil down to one and a half bowls; chop finely, and add half an ounce each of Ren Shen and Dang Gui. Simmer until reduced to eight portions, consume the kidneys on an empty stomach, and drink the juice down. The remaining residue should be dried and ground into powder, formed into a paste with yam powder, shaped like mung beans, taking fifty pills each time, washed down with jujube soup. Two doses will suffice for a cure; this is Master Kunshan’s method. Additionally, add two pennies of frankincense.

    For fright and palpitations with nocturnal emissions: mix fried wooden buns and white qian niu in equal parts to make powder, taking two pennies each time, and administer with rice drink.

    For insufficient heart energy accompanied by erratic palpitations: take two sheng of Jing Li, simmer slowly to extract one sheng, dividing this into warm doses of four he each, taken three times by day and once at night.

    For fright entering the heart causing muteness: decoct Mi Tuo Seng and take a spoonful each time. If powdered, mix with tea and take a pinch.[89p]

    　　自然铜，止惊悸，以酒摩服。 【《大明》】
    　　惊悸善忘，心脏不安，上膈风热，化痰安神：白石英、朱砂各一两为散，每服半钱，食后，煎金银汤下。【《济众方》】
    　　虚劳惊悸，补虚止惊，令人能食：紫石英五两，打如豆大，水淘一遍，以水一斗，煮取三升，细细服，或煮粥食，水尽可再煎之。【张文仲方】
    　　安魂定魄：真珠末豆大一粒，蜜一蚬壳，和服，日三。尤宜小儿。 【《肘后方》】
    　　因惊忧怖迫，或激愤惆怅，致志气错越，心行违僻者：白雄鸡一只，治如食法，真珠四两，薤白四两，水三升，煮二升，尽食之，饮汁令尽。【《肘后方》】
    　　人魄，镇心安神魄，定惊怖癫狂，磨水服之。 【时珍】
    　　伤寒心悸脉结代者：甘草二两，水三升，煮一半，服七合，日一服。 【《类要》，下同】
    　　惊怖卒死：温酒灌之，即醒。[90p]

    Natural copper alleviates palpitations, to be applied with wine.

    For palpitations and forgetfulness, with an unsettled heart and phlegm due to wind-heat in the upper diaphragm: mix one tael each of white quartz and cinnabar into a powder, take half a qian after meals, decoct in gold and silver soup.

    To soothe the spirit and stabilize the soul: one grain of pearl powder about the size of a bean, mixed with honey in a clam shell, taken three times a day—especially suitable for children.

    In cases of fright, worry, or agitation, causing erratic emotions and disordered heart rhythms: take one white rooster prepared as per dietary method, four taels of pearls, four taels of scallion white, three sheng of water, boil down to two sheng, consume entirely along with the broth.

    For the spirit of a person, to settle the heart and calm the spirit, particularly for fear, madness, and frenzy: ground into water and taken.

    For palpitations with a pulse that is knotted and alternate in cases of cold damage: two taels of licorice, three sheng of water, boil down to half, take seven portions each day.

    For sudden death due to fright: warm wine can be administered to revive.[90p]

    　　伤寒发狂，惊怖恍惚：用撒法郎二分，水一盏，浸一夕服之。天方国人所传。 【《医林集要》】
    　　心孔惛塞，多忘善误：丁酉日自至市，买远志裹着衣中角头，还为末服之，勿令人知，不复忘。【《千金》】
    　　健忘，久服聪明益智慧：用白龙骨、远志等分为末，食后酒服方寸匕，日三。《永类钤方》用生姜汤下。【《千金》】
    　　痰迷心窍，心胆被惊，神不守舍，恍惚健忘，妄言妄见：天南星一斤，先掘土坑一尺，以炭火三十斤烧赤，入酒五升渗干，乃安南星在内，盆覆定，以灰塞之，勿令走气。次日取出为末，琥珀一两，朱砂二两为末，生姜汁打面糊，丸梧子大，每服三十丸至五十丸，煎人参石菖蒲汤，一日三服。【《局方》】
    　　治好忘，久服聪明：七月七日，取菖蒲，酒服三方寸匕，饮不至醉。 【《千金》，下同】　　又方：常以甲子日取石上菖蒲一寸九节者，阴干百日，治合下筛，服方寸匕，日三，耳目聪明不忘。[91p]

    1. For delirium caused by febrile diseases, fearful and confused: use two fen of saffrol, one cup of water, soak overnight and take it. This is transmitted from the people of Tianfang.

The next day, take it out and grind it into powder, adding one liang of amber and two liang of cinnabar also ground into powder, mix with ginger juice to make a paste, form into balls the size of walnuts, taking thirty to fifty balls each time, and decoct in ginseng and Acorus calamus soup, taking three times a day.

    　　治人心昏塞，多忘喜误：七月七日，取蜘蛛网着衣领中，勿令人知，不忘。　　又方：七月七日收麻勃一升，人参二两为末，蒸令气遍，每临卧服一刀圭，能尽知四方之事。此乃治健忘，服之能记四方事也。陶云：逆知未来事，过言矣。

    To treat a foggy and blocked mind, which often leads to forgetfulness: On the seventh day of the seventh month, take spider webs and place them in the collar of your clothing without letting others know, and do not forget.

    　　　　针灸

    　　《素问》曰：肺疟者，令人心寒，寒甚热，热间善惊，如有所见者，刺手太阴阳明。　　肝热病者，小便先黄，腹痛多卧，身热，热争则狂言及惊，胁满痛，手足躁，不得安卧。庚辛甚，甲乙大汗。气逆则庚辛死。刺足厥阴少阳。其逆则头痛员员，脉引冲头也。　　无刺大惊人。
    　　人有所堕坠，恶血留内，腹中胀满，不得前后，先饮利药，此上伤厥阴之脉，下伤少阴之络，刺足内踝之下然谷之前血脉出血，刺足跗上动脉；不已，刺三毛上各一痏，见血立已。左刺右，右刺左。善悲惊不乐，刺如右方。　　《灵枢经》曰：热病，嗌干多饮，善惊，卧不能起，取之肤肉，以第六针，五十九。目眦青，索肉于脾，不得索之木，木者肝也。　　热病数惊，瘈瘲而狂，取之脉，以第四针，急泻有余者。[94p]

    Acupuncture

    The "Su Wen" states: In the case of lung malaria, it causes the heart to feel cold, greatly cold with alternating heat, leading to panic and fright as if seeing something. One should prick the hand taiyin and yangming. For liver heat sickness, the urine first turns yellow, there is abdominal pain with much lying down, body heat, and when the heat is intense, there is madness and shock, fullness and pain in the flank, and restlessness in the limbs. If it reaches a severe state, there will be excessive sweating. If qi is reversed, it may lead to death. Prick the foot jueyin and shaoyang. If backward, it causes persistent headaches, with the pulse rising to the head. Do not prick those who are severely frightened.

    If a person has fallen and has retained evil blood inside, with abdominal distension and inability to move forward or backward, first administer a mild laxative. This affects the jueyin pulse above and injures the shaoyin channel below. Prick below the inner ankle, where blood vessels emerge, and prick the artery on the top of the foot; if this does not alleviate, prick three points each on the upper parts until blood is drawn. Prick the left first, then the right, and vice versa. Those who are often saddened, frightened, or melancholic should be pricked according to the right method. The "Ling Shu" states: In heat illness, with dry throat and much drinking, and frequent shock, where one cannot rise from lying down, prick the skin and flesh, using the sixth needle at fifty-nine. If the eyes are blue in the corners, seek flesh from the spleen, not from wood, as wood pertains to the liver.

    In heat illness with multiple shocks, and delirium with mania, check the pulse and use the fourth needle for urgent drainage in cases of excess.[94p]

    癫疾毛发去，索血于心，不得索之水，水者肾也。　　厥头痛，意善忘，按之不得，取头面左右动脉，后取足太阴。《甲乙经》曰：心痛，善悲，厥逆，悬心如饥之状，心憺憺而惊，大陵及间使主之。　　心憺憺而善惊恐，心悲，内关主之。　　善惊悲不乐，厥胫足下热，面尽热渴，行间主之。　　惊，善悲不乐，如堕坠，汗不出，面尘黑，病饮不欲食，照海主之。　　胆眩寒厥，手臂痛，善惊忘言，面赤泣出，腋门主之。　　狐疝惊悸，少气，巨阙主之。[95p]

    The hair falls out due to madness, drawing blood from the heart, unable to draw from water, and water pertains to the kidneys.

    For a headache with cold extremities, one forgets easily; pressing it does not help. Take the arteries on the left and right sides of the head and then the foot's Taiyin.

    The "Jia Yi Classic" states: Heart pain, prone to sadness, with cold extremities, the heart hangs like one who is hungry, feeling restless and surprised, governed by the Daling and Jianshi points.

    When the heart is restless and prone to fear, with sadness, the Neiguan point governs it.

    Prone to fear and sadness, lacking joy, with heat below the calves, the face feels hot and thirsty; the Xingjian point governs it.

    In surprise, with sadness and lack of joy as if falling, sweat does not emerge, and the face turns dark; the Zhaohai point governs it.

    For cold dizziness in the gallbladder with cold limbs, pain in the arms, prone to surprise and loss of words, the face turns red and tears flow; the Yimen point governs it.

    For fright and palpitations, short of breath, the Juque point governs it.[95p]

    　　少腹疝，卧善惊，气海主之。
    　　热病汗不出，鼽衄眩，时仆，面浮肿，足胫寒，不得卧，振寒，恶人与木音，喉痹，龋齿，恶风，鼻不利多善惊，厉兑主之。　　惊不得眠，善断水气上下五脏游气也，三阴交主之。　　《千金方》曰：阳谷，主风眩惊，手卷泄风，汗出，腰项急。　　列缺，主热癎，惊而有所见。
    　　曲骨、阴谷、行间，主惊癎狂走，癫疾。　　间使，主善悲惊狂，面赤目黄，喑不能言。　　阳溪、天井，主惊瘈。[96p]

    　　悬厘、束骨，主癫疾互引，善惊羊鸣。　　天冲，主头痛癫疾互引，数惊悸。
    　　支正、鱼际、合谷、少海、曲池、腕骨，主狂言惊恐。　　阴蹺，主卧惊，视如见鬼。
    　　曲泽、太陵，主心下憺憺，喜惊。
    　　阴交、气海、大巨，主惊不得卧。

    Suspended Li and Bundled Bone are associated with episodic epilepsy and can elicit startled responses like sheep bleating. Tian Chong pertains to headaches and episodic epilepsy, often accompanied by frequent palpitations.

    　　天府、曲地、列缺、百会，主恶风邪气，泣出喜忘。　　左手关上阳绝者，无胆脉也，苦膝疼，口中苦，眯目善畏，如见鬼，多惊少力，刺足厥阴治阴，在足大指间，或刺三毛中。　　《医学纲目》曰：心烁烁跳动，少冲泻之，灸立效。　　健忘，取列缺、心俞、神门、中脘、三里，灸少海。
    　　　　医案

    　　《本事方》曰：绍兴癸丑，予待次四明，有董生者，患神气不宁，每卧则魂飞扬，觉身在床而神魂离体，惊悸多魇，通夕无寐。更医不效，予为诊视。询之曰：医作何病治？董曰：众皆以为心病。予曰：以脉言之，肝经受邪，非心病也。肝气因虚邪气袭之，肝藏魂者也，游魂为变。平人肝不受邪，卧则魂归于肝，神静而得寐。今肝有邪，魂不得归，是以卧则魂飞扬若离体也。肝主怒，故小怒则剧。董欣然曰：前此未之闻，虽未服药，已觉沉疴去体矣。[98p]

    Heavenly Repository, Curved Earth, Hidden Gaps, Hundred Meetings; these govern malevolent winds and evil energies, causing tears of joy to be forgotten.

    When the left hand closes the passage of Yang (which means it relates to vitality), there is no gallbladder pulse, yielding knee pain, bitterness in the mouth, squinting eyes in fear as if seeing ghosts, experiencing many scares and little strength. Needling the foot's Jue Yin point (which is associated with the liver) treats the Yin; this is done between the big toe or at the middle of the three hair folicles (in the foot).

    "The Comprehensive Guide to Medicine" states: when the heart is flickering and beating rapidly, reducing the flow, moxibustion works effectively. For forgetfulness, use the points of the Hidden Gaps, Heart Shu, Spirit Gate, Central Pass, and Three Miles, and moxibustion on the Lesser Sea.

    Case Study

    "The Fundamental Prescriptions" states: In the year of the Gui Chou of Shaoxing, I was in the city of Siming, where a man named Dong suffered from unsettled spirit energy. Each time he lay down, his soul would soar, sensing his body in bed but his spirit detached. He experienced fright and many nightmares, unable to sleep throughout the night. Other doctors were ineffective, so I proceeded to diagnose him. I asked: "What kind of illness did the doctors treat?" Dong replied, "Everyone thinks it’s a heart illness." I said: "From the pulse, the liver channel is afflicted, so it is not a heart illness. The liver energy is attacked by deficient evil energy. The liver stores the soul; when the wandering spirit changes, the healthy person’s liver does not suffer from evil and allows the soul to return to the liver efficiently, thus achieving calmness and sleep. Now, with evil in the liver, the soul cannot return, so while lying down, it feels as though the soul is soaring outside the body." The liver governs anger, thus even a little anger feels severe. Dong joyfully said: "I have never heard this explanation before. Although I have not taken any medicine, I already feel my chronic illness beginning to leave my body."[98p]

    愿求治之！予曰：公且持此说，与众医议治之方而徐质之。阅旬日，复至。云医遍议古今方，无与病相对者。故余处以真珠母丸、独活汤二方以赠服，一月而病悉除。此方用真珠母为君，龙齿佐之。真珠母人肝经为第一，龙齿与肝同类也。龙齿、虎睛，今人例以为镇心药，殊不知龙齿安魂，虎睛定魄，各言其类也。盖东方苍龙，木也，属肝而藏魂。西方白虎，金也，属肺而藏魄。龙能变化，故魂游而不定；虎能专静，故魄止而有守。予谓治魄不宁者，宜以虎睛；治魂飞扬者，宜以龙齿。万物有成理而不失，在夫人达之而已矣。[99p]

    I wish to seek treatment! I said: You should hold on to this statement and discuss it with other physicians regarding the method of treatment and then gradually inquire further. After ten days, you came back. You said that the physicians thoroughly discussed both ancient and modern formulas, but none corresponded to the illness. Therefore, I prescribed the Pearl Mother Pill and the Du Huo Decoction for you, and after a month, the illness was completely cured. This treatment uses Pearl Mother as the chief ingredient and Dragon's Tooth as an assistant. Pearl Mother primarily belongs to the liver channel, and Dragon's Tooth is similarly related to the liver. Dragon's Tooth and Tiger's Eye are often regarded by modern people as heart-calming medicines, yet they do not realize that Dragon's Tooth soothes the soul, while Tiger's Eye stabilizes the spirit, each referring to its nature. The eastern Azure Dragon represents wood, belonging to the liver, where the soul is housed. The western White Tiger represents metal, belonging to the lungs, where the spirit is housed. The dragon is capable of transformation, thus the soul wanders and remains undetermined; the tiger maintains composure, allowing the spirit to rest and be guarded. I believe to treat an unsettled spirit, one should use Tiger's Eye; to treat a wandering soul, one should use Dragon's Tooth. All things have a natural order which does not change, but it relies on individuals to comprehend it.[99p]

    　　《儒门事亲》曰：卫德新之妻，旅中宿于楼上，夜值盗劫人烧舍，惊堕床下。自后每闻有响，则惊倒不知人，家人辈蹑足而行，莫敢冒触有声，岁余不痊，诸医作心病治之。人参、珍珠及定志丸皆无效。戴人见而断之曰：惊者为阳，从外入也；恐者为阴，从内出也。惊者为自不知，恐者自知也。足少阳胆经属肝木，胆者敢也，惊怕则胆伤矣。乃命二侍女执其两手，按高椅之上，当面前下置一小几。戴人曰：娘子当视此。一木猛击之，其妇大惊。戴人曰：我以木击几，何以惊乎？伺少定，击之，惊乃缓。又斯须连击三五次，又以杖击门，又暗遣入画背后之窗，徐徐惊定而笑曰：是何治法？戴人曰：《内经》云：惊者平之，平者常也。平常见之，必无惊。是夜使人击其门窗，自夕达曙。夫惊者神上越也，从下击几，使之下视，所以收神也。一二日虽闻雷亦不惊。德新素不喜戴人，至是终身敬服，如有人言戴人不知医者，执戈以逐之。[100p]

    The "Ruzhong Shiqin" states: Wei Dexin’s wife was staying overnight on a second floor while traveling, when thieves attacked and set fire to the place, causing her to fall from the bed in fright. From then on, whenever she heard a sound, she would be startled and unaware of people around her, and her family members would walk on tiptoe, daring not to make a sound. For over a year, she did not recover, and various doctors diagnosed her condition as a heart illness, treating her with ginseng, pearls, and calming pills, all without effect.

    A healer observed her condition and concluded: "Fright comes from outside; it is yang. Fear arises from within; it is yin. Fright is due to a lack of self-awareness, while fear comes from self-awareness. The gallbladder, belonging to the liver’s wood element, represents courage. If someone is frightened, it harms the gallbladder." He then instructed two maids to hold her hands and positioned a small table in front of her on a high chair. The healer said, "Madam, you should look at this." He struck a piece of wood against the table, causing her to be greatly startled. The healer remarked, "I struck the table with a piece of wood; why are you startled?" After a moment of calm, he struck again, and her fright lessened. Again, he struck three to five more times, hit the door with a staff, and quietly sent someone to knock on the window behind a painting, gradually helping her calm down and laugh, saying, "What is this treatment method?"

    The healer replied: "The Inner Canon states: ‘Fright should be settled; settlement leads to normalcy.’ When one regularly encounters such things, there will be no fright." That night, he had someone knock on her doors and windows from dusk until dawn. For the frightened person, the spirit is elevated. By striking the table from below, she looks down, thus retrieving her spirit. After just a day or two, even if she heard thunder, she would not be frightened. Dexin had never liked the healer, but from then on, he respected him for life, to the extent that if anyone said the healer was incompetent in medicine, he would take up arms against them.[100p]

    　　新寨马叟年五十九，因秋欠税，官杖六十，得惊气，成风搐已三年矣。病大发则手足颤掉，不能持物，食则令人代哺，口目张腅，唇舌嚼烂，抖擞之状，如线引傀儡，每发，市人皆聚观。夜卧发热，衣被尽去，遍身燥痒，中热而反外寒，久欲自尽，手不能绳，倾产求医，至破其家而病益坚。叟之子，邑中旧小吏也，以父病讯戴人。戴人曰：此病甚易治。若隆暑时不过一涌，再涌夺则愈矣。今已秋寒，可三之。如未愈，更刺腧穴必愈。先以通圣散汗之，继服涌剂则吐痰一二升，至晚又下五七行，其疾小愈。待五日，再一涌出痰三四升，如鸡蛋黄成块状，如汤热。叟以手颤不能自探，妻与代探，咽嗌肿伤，昏愦如醉，约一二时许，稍稍省，又下数行，立觉势轻颤减，热亦不作，足亦能步，手能巾栉，自持匙箸，未至三涌，病去如濯。病后但觉极寒，戴人曰：当以食补之，久则自退。盖大疾之去，卫气未复，故宜以散风导气之药。切不可以热剂温之，反成他病。[101p]

    The old man from the new village was fifty-nine years old. Due to a tax debt in autumn, he was hit with the official staff sixty times, which left him in shock and gave him a wind issue that had lasted for three years. When the illness intensified, his hands and feet trembled uncontrollably, rendering him unable to hold objects. He required someone to feed him, his mouth and eyes became dull, and his lips and tongue were in a sorry state. His trembling was like a marionette being pulled by strings, and whenever he had an episode, people in the market would gather to watch. At night, he experienced fever, discarding his clothes and bedding, with his whole body itching. He felt hot inside but cold outside, and for a long time wanted to end his life but couldn't even manage that. He sought medical help to the point of exhausting his family, yet his illness worsened.

    The old man's son, a minor official in the town, informed a healer about his father's condition. The healer said that this illness was quite easy to treat. If it were still the peak of summer, a single eruption would suffice to cure him. Now that it was autumn and cooler, he suggested that three eruptions might be needed. If he did not get better, the healer could further stimulate acupuncture points to ensure recovery. They first used a sweat-inducing powder to promote perspiration, then administered an eruptive remedy that caused him to expel one or two liters of phlegm. By evening, he would also experience five to seven bowel movements, which slightly improved his condition.

    After five days, another eruption expelled three to four liters of phlegm, resembling clumps of egg yolk and appearing as hot as soup. The old man, unable to observe this himself due to his shaking hands, had his wife check. His throat was swollen and painful, leaving him dazed like a drunk. After about an hour or two, he gradually regained some consciousness and had several more bowel movements. He immediately felt lighter, his trembling reduced, the fever subsided, and he could walk again. His hands regained the ability to hold a comb and a spoon. Before three eruptions occurred, his illness vanished as if washed away.

    After recovering, he only felt extreme cold. The healer advised him to nourish himself with food, which would gradually help him recover. Indeed, after a major illness passes, the protective qi is not fully restored, so it is advisable to use medicines that dispel wind and guide qi. It is crucial not to use hot remedies to warm him, as that could lead to other ailments.[101p]

    　　上渠卜家一男子，年二十八岁，病身弱，四肢无力，面色苍黄，左胁下身侧上下如臂状，每发则痛无时，食不减，大便如常，小便微黄，已二三载矣。诸医计穷，求戴人治之。视其部分，乃足厥阴肝经，兼足少阳胆经也。张曰：甲胆乙肝，故青，其黄者脾也。诊胆脉小，此因惊也。惊则胆受邪，腹中当有惊涎绿水。病人曰：昔曾屯军被火，自是而疾。戴人夜以舟车百五十丸，浚川散四五钱加生姜自然汁，平旦果下绿水四五行。或问：大加生姜何也？答曰：辛能伐木也。下后觉微痛，令再下之，比前药减三之一。又下绿水三四行，痛止思食，反有力。戴人谓卜曰：汝妻亦当病。[102p]

    A man, twenty-eight years old, sought treatment. He was weak, with limp limbs and a pale complexion. He felt pain in the left side of his body, radiating like an arm, with pain occurring at all times. His appetite was not diminished, his bowel movements were normal, and his urine was slightly yellow. This had persisted for two or three years. Various doctors had exhausted their methods and sought the help of a healer. Upon examination, it was found that the issue involved the foot Jueyin liver channel and was also related to the foot Shaoyang gallbladder channel. The healer stated: "The liver corresponds to wood, and the gallbladder to fire; thus the green. The yellow represents the spleen." He diagnosed a weak gallbladder pulse, indicating a shock. Due to this shock, the gallbladder was afflicted, and there should be green phlegm in the abdomen. The patient mentioned that he had previously been in a military camp that caught fire, which marked the onset of his illness. The healer prepared one hundred fifty pills of Juanchuan powder, adding four to five qian of ginger juice, to be taken in the early morning. After ingestion, the patient expelled green phlegm four to five times. When asked about the large quantity of ginger, the healer replied: "The spicy nature can cut through stagnation." After expelling phlegm, the patient felt slight pain and was instructed to expel once more, this time using a dosage reduced by one-third. He expelled green phlegm three to four times, after which the pain stopped, and he felt hungry and regained some strength. The healer then remarked to the patient: "Your wife is also likely to be ill."[102p]

    卜曰：太医未见吾妻，何以知之？曰：尔感此惊几年矣？卜省曰：当被火时，我正在草堂中熟睡，人惊唤，我睡中惊不能言，火已塞门，我父拽出我火中，今五年矣。张曰：汝胆伏大惊，甲乙乘脾土，是少阳相火乘脾，脾中有热，故能食而杀谷，热虽能化谷，其精气不完，汝必无子。盖败精反损妇人，汝妻必手足热，四肢无力，经血不时。卜曰：吾妻实如此，亦已五年矣。他日，门人因观《内经》言先泻所不胜次泻所胜之论，其法何如以问张。张曰，且如胆木乘胃土，此土不胜木也。不胜之气，寻救于子，己土能生庚金，庚为大肠，味辛者为金，故大加生姜使伐木。然先不开脾土，无由行也。遂用舟车丸先通其闭塞之路，是先泻其所不胜，后用姜汁调浚川散大下之，次泻其所胜也。大抵阳干克阳干，腑克腑，脏克脏。[103p]

    The divination said: The chief physician has not seen my wife, how can he know? He replied: How long have you been affected by this shock? The diviner reflected and said: When the fire struck, I was fast asleep in the cottage. I was startled awake by my family calling out, but I couldn't speak due to the shock; by then the fire had blocked the door, and my father pulled me out from the flames. It has been five years since then. Zhang said: Your courage is weakened by the great fright; the liver (gallbladder) is dominating the spleen (earth). This means the lesser yang fire is overpowering the spleen, and there is heat in the spleen, which destroys the grains you eat. Although the heat can transform the grains, the essence is not preserved, hence you will surely have no children. This causes the essence to fail and adversely affects the woman as well; therefore, your wife must have heat in her limbs, weakness in her extremities, and irregular menstrual flow. The diviner replied: My wife is indeed like this; it has also been five years. On another day, a disciple asked Zhang about the theory found in the "Inner Canon" regarding the relations of excess and deficiency in treatments. Zhang said: For instance, if wood affects the earth of the stomach, this earth cannot overcome the wood. The deficient energy seeks refuge in the child; the earth can generate metal (geng), which corresponds to the large intestine, while the spicy flavors represent metal; thus one uses a great quantity of ginger to overcome the wood. However, one must not first open the earth of the spleen, as it will not be able to function that way. Therefore, one first uses herbal pills to clear the blocked pathway, which treats what cannot be overcome first, and then ginger juice is used to enhance the laxative effect for subsequent treatment of what is overcome. Generally speaking, yang overcomes yang, the organs influence the organs, and the viscera influence the viscera.[103p]

    　　《丹溪心法》曰：宪幕之子傅兄年十七八，时暑月因劳而渴，恣饮梅浆，又连得大惊三四次，妄言妄见，病似邪鬼。诊其脉，两手皆虚弦而带沉数。余曰：数为有热，虚弦是大惊，又梅酸之浆郁于中脘，补虚清热，导去痰滞，病乃可安。遂与人参、白朮、陈皮、茯苓、芩、连等浓煎汤，入竹沥、姜汁，与旬日未效。众皆尤药之不审。余脉之，知其虚之未完与痰之未导也。仍与前方，入荆沥，又旬日而安。[104p]

    The "Danxi Heart Method" states: The son of Xianmu, Brother Fu, was around seventeen or eighteen years old. During the hot summer months, he became thirsty from exertion and excessively drank plum juice. Subsequently, he experienced three or four severe shocks, leading to delusions and hallucinations, as if afflicted by evil spirits. Upon examining his pulse, both hands exhibited a weak and string-like quality along with a heavy, rapid beat. I noted that the rapidity indicated heat, the weak and string-like quality pointed to severe shock, and the sour plum juice had stagnated in the middle burner. Therefore, to replenish the deficiency, clear the heat, and guide away the phlegm, the illness could be stabilized. I prescribed a concentrated decoction of ginseng, white atractylodes, dried tangerine peel, poria, radish root, and lotus seeds, and added bamboo juice and ginger juice to it. After ten days without effect, the others speculated on the ineffectiveness of the medicine. After examining the pulse again, I recognized the deficiency had not been fully addressed and phlegm had not been expelled. I continued with the original formula and added a decoction of windbreaker (Jingli) and after another ten days, he was stable.[104p]

    　　《医学纲目》曰：林学士本南人，历内地为官，有一子甚端严而聪敏，父母爱之，居常喜食海蛤，饮食之顷，未尝不设，至十八年，忽面色顿青，形体瘦削，夜多惊悸，皆谓劳瘵之疾，百疗不瘳，遂召杜脉之。杜曰：非病。何以知之，盖虽病削面青，精神不减，问秀才好食甚物？曰：多食南海中味。杜曰：但多服生津液药，病当自愈。如是经两月，面色渐有红润意，夜亦无惊悸。林问曰：医师之验，久闻世名，愿闻此病所以。杜曰：王冰注《素问》曰：盐发渴，乃胜血之证。海味皆咸物，既多食海味，使心血渐衰，则夜惊悸。今既去咸，用生津液之药，人且少壮，血液易生，面色渐有红润，此疾去乃安矣。众医以为劳瘵，非其治也。[105p]

    The "Medical Essentials" states: Scholar Lin was originally from the south and served as an official in the interior. He had a son who was very respectful and intelligent. His parents cherished him and often enjoyed eating sea clams; they would set them out at meals without fail. When the son turned eighteen, his complexion suddenly turned pale and his body became emaciated. He often experienced fright and restlessness at night, and everyone thought he suffered from a wasting disease. Despite numerous treatments, he did not improve, so they called in Du Maizhi. Du said: "It is not a disease." When asked how he knew, he explained: "Although his face is pale and he is emaciated, his spirit remains undiminished. Ask the young scholar what he likes to eat." The scholar replied: "I particularly enjoy eating various sea delicacies." Du said: "If you consume too many salty foods from the sea, it will cause thirst, which is a sign of blood depletion. Since you eat so much salty food, your heart and blood gradually weaken, leading to fright and restlessness at night. Now that you've avoided salty foods and are using medicines to generate body fluids, since one is still young, blood replenishment will be easier, and your complexion will gradually regain its reddish hue. Once this condition is resolved, you will find peace." The other physicians believed it to be a wasting disease, but that was not the correct treatment.[105p]

    　　《薛己医案》曰：下堡顾仁成年六十有一，痢后入房，精滑自遗，二日方止。又房劳感寒怒气，遂发寒热，右胁痛连心胸，腹痞，自汗盗汗如雨，四肢厥冷，睡中惊悸，或觉上升如浮，或觉下陷如堕，遂致废寝。或用补药二剂益甚。脉浮大洪数，按之微细，此属无火虚热，急与十全大补加山药、山茱、丹皮、附子一剂，诸证顿愈而痊。此等元气百无一二。
    [106p]

    The "Case Records of Xue Ji" states: Gu Ren, a resident of Xiabao, is sixty-one years old. After suffering from diarrhea, he entered the bedroom, leading to involuntary emission for two days. Subsequently, he felt cold due to excessive sexual activity, which resulted in chills and fevers, pain in the right side affecting the heart and chest, abdominal distension, spontaneous sweating, and profuse night sweats. His limbs became cold, and he experienced frightful dreams while sleeping; at times he felt a rising sensation as if floating, and at other times a sinking feeling as if falling, which caused him to lose sleep. Taking two doses of tonic medicine only made it worse. His pulse was floating, large, and rapid; upon pressing, it felt weak and fine. This indicated a lack of fire and a deficiency of heat. I urgently prescribed a dose of "Ten Complete Tonics" with added Chinese yam, shan zhu yu, dan pi, and fu zi. All symptoms promptly improved, leading to recovery. Such are the vital energies that can rarely go wrong.[106p]
